<p>The <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Union_and_Progress" title="Committee of Union and Progress">Committee of Union and Progress</a> founded the "Special Organization" (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <span lang="tr"><i>Teşkilât-ı Mahsusa</i></span>) that participated in the destruction of the Ottoman Armenian community.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[84]</a></sup> This organization adopted its name in 1913 and functioned like a special forces outfit, and it has been compared by some scholars to the Nazi <a href="/wiki/Einsatzgruppen" title="Einsatzgruppen">Einsatzgruppen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Balakian_42-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Balakian-42">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:182, 185</sup> Later in 1914, the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Government_(Ottoman_Empire)" title="Imperial Government (Ottoman Empire)">Ottoman government</a> influenced the direction the Special Organization was to take by releasing criminals from central prisons to be the central elements of this newly formed Special Organization.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[85]</a></sup> According to the Mazhar commissions attached to the tribunal as soon as November 1914, 124 criminals were released from Pimian prison. Little by little from the end of 1914 to the beginning of 1915, hundreds, then thousands of prisoners were freed to form the members of this organization. Later, they were charged with escorting the convoys of Armenian deportees.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[86]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vehib_Pasha" class="mw-redirect" title="Vehib Pasha">Vehib Pasha</a>, commander of the Ottoman Third Army, called those members of the Special Organization the "butchers of the human species".<sup id="cite_ref-Lewy_2005_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewy_2005-90">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Massacres">Massacres</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_burnings">Mass burnings</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Morgenthau336.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Morgenthau336.jpg/220px-Morgenthau336.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Morgenthau336.jpg/330px-Morgenthau336.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Morgenthau336.jpg/440px-Morgenthau336.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3999" data-file-height="2731" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Morgenthau336.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Morgenthau's caption: "Those who fell by the wayside. Scenes like this were common all over the Armenian provinces in the spring and summer months of 1915. Death in its several forms—massacre, starvation, exhaustion—destroyed the larger part of the refugees. The Turkish policy was that of extermination under the guise of deportation".<sup id="cite_ref-Morgenthau_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morgenthau-57">[54]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Eitan Belkind was a <a href="/wiki/Nili" title="Nili">Nili</a> member who infiltrated the Ottoman army as an official. He was assigned to the headquarters of Kemal Pasha. He claims to have witnessed the burning of 5,000 Armenians.<sup id="cite_ref-Auron_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auron-91">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:181, 183</sup></p>
<p>Lt. Hasan Maruf of the Ottoman army describes how a population of a village were taken all together and then burned.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[89]</a></sup> The Commander of the Third Army Vehib's 12-page <a href="/wiki/Affidavit" title="Affidavit">affidavit</a>, which was dated 5 December 1918, was presented in the Trabzon trial series (29 March 1919) included in the Key Indictment,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[90]</a></sup> reporting such a mass burning of the population of an entire village near <a href="/wiki/Mu%C5%9F" title="Muş">Muş</a>: "The shortest method for disposing of the women and children concentrated in the various camps was to burn them".<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[91]</a></sup> Further, it was reported that "Turkish prisoners who had apparently witnessed some of these scenes were horrified and maddened at remembering the sight. They told the Russians that the stench of the burning human flesh permeated the air for many days after".<sup id="cite_ref-Bryce_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bryce-95">[92]</a></sup> Vahakn Dadrian wrote that 80,000 Armenians in 90 villages across the Muş plain were burned in "stables and haylofts".<sup id="cite_ref-charny95_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charny95-96">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Drowning">Drowning</span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Trabzon" title="Trabzon">Trabzon</a> was the main city in Trabzon province; <a href="/wiki/Oscar_S._Heizer" title="Oscar S. Heizer">Oscar S. Heizer</a>, the American consul at Trabzon, reported: "This plan did not suit Nail Bey&#160;... Many of the children were loaded into boats and taken out to sea and thrown overboard".<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[94]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hafiz_Mehmet" class="mw-redirect" title="Hafiz Mehmet">Hafiz Mehmet</a>, a Turkish deputy serving Trabzon, testified during a 21 December 1918 parliamentary session of the Chamber of Deputies that "the district's governor loaded the Armenians into barges and had them thrown overboard."<sup id="cite_ref-Winter2004_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Winter2004-98">[95]</a></sup> The Italian consul of Trabzon in 1915, <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Gorrini" title="Giacomo Gorrini">Giacomo Gorrini</a>, writes: "I saw thousands of innocent women and children placed on boats which were capsized in the Black Sea".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[96]</a></sup> Vahakn Dadrian places the number of Armenians killed in the Trabzon province by drowning at 50,000.<sup id="cite_ref-charny95_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charny95-96">[93]</a></sup> The Trabzon trials reported Armenians having been drowned in the Black Sea;<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[97]</a></sup> according to a testimony, women and children were loaded on boats in "Değirmendere" to be drowned in the sea.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAk.C3.A7am2012312_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAk.C3.A7am2012312-101">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hoffman Philip, the American <i><a href="/wiki/Charg%C3%A9_d%27affaires" title="Chargé d'affaires">chargé d'affaires</a></i> at Constantinople, wrote: "Boat loads sent from Zor down the river arrived at Ana, one thirty miles away, with three fifths of passengers missing".<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[99]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Robert_Fisk" title="Robert Fisk">Robert Fisk</a>, 900 Armenian women were drowned in Bitlis, while in Erzincan, the corpses in the Euphrates resulted in a change of course of the river for a few hundred meters.<sup id="cite_ref-Fisk_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fisk-65">[62]</a></sup> Dadrian also wrote that "countless" Armenians were drowned in the Euphrates and its tributaries.<sup id="cite_ref-charny95_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charny95-96">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_of_poison_and_drug_overdoses">Use of poison and drug overdoses</span></h4>
<p>The psychiatrist Robert Jay Lifton writes in a parenthesis when introducing the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust#Medical_experiments" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">medical experiments during the Holocaust</a>, "Perhaps Turkish doctors, in their participation in the genocide against the Armenians, come closest, as I shall later suggest".<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Morphine" title="Morphine">Morphine</a> overdose:</b> During the Trabzon trial series of the Martial court, from the sittings between 26 March and 17 May 1919, the Trabzons Health Services Inspector Dr. Ziya Fuad wrote in a report that Dr. Saib caused the death of children with the injection of morphine. The information was allegedly provided by two physicians (Drs. Ragib and Vehib), both Dr. Saib's colleagues at Trabzons Red Crescent hospital, where those atrocities were said to have been committed.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p><b>Toxic gas:</b> Dr. Ziya Fuad and Dr. Adnan, public health services director of Trabzon, submitted affidavits reporting cases in which two school buildings were used to organize children and send them to the mezzanine to kill them with toxic gas equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-turkishdoctors_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turkishdoctors-106">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p><b>Typhoid <a href="/wiki/Inoculation" title="Inoculation">inoculation</a>:</b> The Ottoman surgeon, Dr. Haydar Cemal wrote "on the order of the Chief Sanitation Office of the Third Army in January 1916, when the spread of <a href="/wiki/Typhus" title="Typhus">typhus</a> was an acute problem, innocent Armenians slated for deportation at Erzincan were inoculated with the blood of typhoid fever patients without rendering that blood 'inactive'".<sup id="cite_ref-turkishdoctors_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turkishdoctors-106">[103]</a></sup> Jeremy Hugh Baron writes: "Individual doctors were directly involved in the massacres, having poisoned infants, killed children and issued false certificates of death from natural causes. <a href="/wiki/Nazim_Bey" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazim Bey">Nazim</a>'s brother-in-law <a href="/wiki/Tevfik_R%C3%BC%C5%9Ft%C3%BC_Aras" title="Tevfik Rüştü Aras">Dr. Tevfik Rushdu</a>, Inspector-General of Health Services, organized the disposal of Armenian corpses with thousands of kilos of lime over six months; he became foreign secretary from 1925 to 1938".<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trials">Trials</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkish_courts-martial">Turkish courts-martial</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Courts-Martial_of_1919%E2%80%9320" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Courts-Martial of 1919–20">Turkish Courts-Martial of 1919–20</a></div>
<p>On the night of 2–3 November 1918 and with the aid of <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Izzet_Pasha" title="Ahmed Izzet Pasha">Ahmed Izzet Pasha</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Three_Pashas" title="Three Pashas">Three Pashas</a></i> (which include Mehmed Talaat Pasha and Ismail Enver, the main perpetrators of the Genocide) fled the Ottoman Empire.</p>
<p>In 1919, after the <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_Mudros" title="Armistice of Mudros">Mudros Armistice</a>, Sultan <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_VI" title="Mehmed VI">Mehmed VI</a> was ordered to organise courts-martial by the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allied administration</a> in charge of Constantinople to try members of the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Union_and_Progress" title="Committee of Union and Progress">Committee of Union and Progress</a> (CUP) (Turkish: "<i>Ittihat ve Terakki</i>") for taking the Ottoman Empire into World War I. By January 1919, a report to Sultan <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_VI" title="Mehmed VI">Mehmed VI</a> accused over 130 suspects, most of whom were high officials.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sultan <a href="/wiki/Mehmet_VI" class="mw-redirect" title="Mehmet VI">Mehmet VI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grand_Vizier" title="Grand Vizier">Grand Vizier</a> <a href="/wiki/Damat_Ferid_Pasha" title="Damat Ferid Pasha">Damat Ferid Pasha</a>, as representatives of <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Government_(Ottoman_Empire)" title="Imperial Government (Ottoman Empire)">government</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Constitutional_Era" title="Second Constitutional Era">Second Constitutional Era</a>, were summoned to the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919" title="Paris Peace Conference, 1919">Paris Peace Conference</a> by <a href="/wiki/US_Secretary_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="US Secretary of State">US Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lansing" title="Robert Lansing">Robert Lansing</a>. On 11 July 1919, <a href="/wiki/Damat_Ferid_Pasha" title="Damat Ferid Pasha">Damat Ferid Pasha</a> officially confessed to massacres against the <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Armenians in the Ottoman Empire">Armenians in the Ottoman Empire</a> and was a key figure and initiator of the war crime <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Courts-Martial_of_1919%E2%80%9320" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Courts-Martial of 1919–20">trials</a> held directly after World War I to condemn to death the chief perpetrators of the Genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[108]</a></sup> The military court found that it was the will of the CUP to eliminate the Armenians physically, via its <a href="/wiki/Special_Organization_(Ottoman_Empire)" title="Special Organization (Ottoman Empire)">Special Organization</a>. The 1919 pronouncement reads as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[109]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/Turkish_Courts-Martial_of_1919%E2%80%9320" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Courts-Martial of 1919–20">The Court Martial</a> taking into consideration the above-named crimes declares, unanimously, the culpability as principal factors of these crimes the fugitives Talaat Pasha, former Grand Vizir, Enver Efendi, former War Minister, struck off the register of the Imperial Army, Cemal Efendi, former Navy Minister, struck off too from the Imperial Army, and Dr. Nazim Efendi, former Minister of Education, members of the General Council of the Union &amp; Progress, representing the moral person of that party;&#160;... the Court Martial pronounces, in accordance with said stipulations of the Law the death penalty against Talaat, Enver, Cemal, and Dr. Nazim.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>After the pronouncement, the <i><a href="/wiki/Three_Pashas" title="Three Pashas">Three Pashas</a></i> were sentenced to death in absentia at the trials in Constantinople. The courts-martial officially disbanded the CUP and confiscated its assets and the assets of those found guilty. The courts-martial were dismissed in August 1920 for their lack of transparency, according to then High Commissioner and Admiral Sir <a href="/wiki/John_de_Robeck" title="John de Robeck">John de Robeck</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-doc136069_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doc136069-113">[110]</a></sup> and some of the accused were transported to <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_Malta" title="Crown Colony of Malta">Malta</a> for further interrogation, only to be released afterwards in an exchange of <a href="/wiki/POW" class="mw-redirect" title="POW">POWs</a>. Two of the three Pashas were later assassinated by Armenian vigilantes during <a href="/wiki/Operation_Nemesis" title="Operation Nemesis">Operation Nemesis</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Detainees_in_Malta">Detainees in Malta</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Effort_to_prosecute_Ottoman_war_criminals" title="Effort to prosecute Ottoman war criminals">Effort to prosecute Ottoman war criminals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malta_exiles" title="Malta exiles">Malta exiles</a></div>
<p>Ottoman military members and high-ranking politicians convicted by the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Courts-Martial_of_1919%E2%80%9320" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Courts-Martial of 1919–20">Turkish courts-martial</a> were transferred from Constantinople prisons to the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_Malta" title="Crown Colony of Malta">Crown Colony of Malta</a> on board of the SS <i>Princess Ena</i> and the HMS <i>Benbow</i> by the British forces, starting in 1919. Admiral Sir <a href="/wiki/Somerset_Gough-Calthorpe" title="Somerset Gough-Calthorpe">Somerset Gough-Calthorpe</a> was in charge of the operation, together with Lord Curzon; they did so owing to the lack of transparency of the Turkish courts-martial. They were held there for three years, while searches were made of archives in Constantinople, London, Paris and Washington to find a way to put them in trial.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[111]</a></sup> However, the war criminals were eventually released without trial and returned to Constantinople in 1921, in exchange for twenty-two British <a href="/wiki/POW" class="mw-redirect" title="POW">prisoners of war</a> held by the government in Ankara, including a relative of Lord Curzon. The government in Ankara was opposed to political power of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Government_(Ottoman_Empire)" title="Imperial Government (Ottoman Empire)">government in Constantinople</a>. They are often mentioned as the <i>Malta exiles</i> in some sources.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBonello2008_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBonello2008-115">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919" title="Paris Peace Conference, 1919">Peace Conference in Paris</a> established the "<i>Commission on Responsibilities and Sanctions</i>" in January 1919, which was commissioned by United States Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lansing" title="Robert Lansing">Robert Lansing</a>. Based on the commission's work, several articles were added to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres" title="Treaty of Sèvres">Treaty of Sèvres</a>. The Treaty of Sèvres had planned a trial in August 1920 to determine those responsible for the "barbarous and illegitimate methods of warfare&#160;... [including] offenses against the laws and customs of war and the principles of humanity".<sup id="cite_ref-nazi_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nazi-29">[26]</a></sup> Article 230 of the Treaty of Sèvres required the Ottoman Empire hand over to the Allied Powers the persons responsible for the massacres committed during the war on August 1, 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Human_Rights" title="European Court of Human Rights">European Court of Human Rights</a> judge <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Bonello" title="Giovanni Bonello">Giovanni Bonello</a> the suspension of prosecution attempts and the release and repatriation of the detainees was, amongst others, a result of the lack of an appropriate legal framework with <a href="/wiki/Jurisdiction" title="Jurisdiction">supranational jurisdiction</a>. Following World War I no international norms for regulating war crimes existed, due to a legal vacuum in international law; therefore (contrary to Turkish sources) no trials were ever held in Malta.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBonello2008_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBonello2008-115">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gbonello_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gbonello-117">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Trial_of_Soghomon_Tehlirian">Trial of Soghomon Tehlirian</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Operation_Nemesis" title="Operation Nemesis">Operation Nemesis</a></div>
<p>On 15 March 1921, former <a href="/wiki/Grand_Vizier" title="Grand Vizier">Grand Vizier</a> <a href="/wiki/Talaat_Pasha" title="Talaat Pasha">Talaat Pasha</a> was assassinated in the <a href="/wiki/Charlottenburg" title="Charlottenburg">Charlottenburg</a> District of Berlin, Germany, in broad daylight and in the presence of many witnesses. Talaat's death was part of "<i><a href="/wiki/Operation_Nemesis" title="Operation Nemesis">Operation Nemesis</a></i>", the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Revolutionary_Federation" title="Armenian Revolutionary Federation">Armenian Revolutionary Federation</a>'s codename for their covert operation in the 1920s to kill the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turks" title="Young Turks">planners</a> of the Armenian Genocide.</p>
<p>The subsequent trial and acquittal of the assassin, <a href="/wiki/Soghomon_Tehlirian" title="Soghomon Tehlirian">Soghomon Tehlirian</a>, had an important influence on <a href="/wiki/Raphael_Lemkin" title="Raphael Lemkin">Raphael Lemkin</a>, a lawyer of <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Polish</a>–<a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> descent who campaigned in the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> to ban what he called "barbarity" and "vandalism". The term "<a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>", created in 1943, was coined by Lemkin who was directly influenced by the massacres of Armenians during World War I.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bloxham_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloxham-119">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:210</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Armenian_population.2C_deaths.2C_survivors.2C_1914_to_1923">Armenian population, deaths, survivors, 1914 to 1923</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bones_of_Armenians.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bones_of_Armenians.jpg/220px-Bones_of_Armenians.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bones_of_Armenians.jpg/330px-Bones_of_Armenians.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bones_of_Armenians.jpg/440px-Bones_of_Armenians.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1401" data-file-height="997" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bones_of_Armenians.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Uncovering the bones of Armenians in Deir ez-Zor.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[117]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Armenian_population" title="Ottoman Armenian population">Ottoman Armenian population</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Armenian_casualties" title="Ottoman Armenian casualties">Ottoman Armenian casualties</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide_survivors" title="Armenian Genocide survivors">Armenian Genocide survivors</a></div>
<p>While there is no consensus as to how many Armenians lost their lives during the Armenian Genocide, there is general agreement among western historians that over 500,000&#160;Armenians died between 1914 and 1918. Estimates vary between 800,000<sup id="cite_ref-Heidenrich2001_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heidenrich2001-121">[118]</a></sup> and 1,500,000 (per the governments of France,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[119]</a></sup> Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[120]</a></sup> and other states). <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Encyclopædia Britannica</a></i> references the research of <a href="/wiki/Arnold_J._Toynbee" title="Arnold J. Toynbee">Arnold J. Toynbee</a>, an intelligence officer of the <a href="/wiki/British_Foreign_Office" class="mw-redirect" title="British Foreign Office">British Foreign Office</a>, who estimated that 600,000&#160;Armenians "died or were massacred during deportation" in a report compiled on 24 May 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-Bryce_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bryce-95">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[121]</a></sup> This figure, however, accounts for solely the first year of the Genocide and does not take into account those who died or were killed after May 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to documents that once belonged to Talaat Pasha, more than 970,000 Ottoman Armenians disappeared from official population records from 1915 through 1916. In 1983, Talaat's widow, Hayriye Talaat Bafralı, gave the documents and records to Turkish journalist <a href="/wiki/Murat_Bardak%C3%A7%C4%B1" title="Murat Bardakçı">Murat Bardakçı</a>, who published them in a book titled <i>The Remaining Documents of Talat Pasha</i> (also known as "Talat Pasha's Black Book"). According to the documents, the number of Armenians living in the Ottoman Empire before 1915 stood at 1,256,000. It was presumed, however, in a footnote by Talaat Pasha himself, that the Armenian population was undercounted by thirty percent. Furthermore, the population of Protestant Armenians was not taken into account. Therefore, according to the historian <a href="/wiki/Ara_Sarafian" title="Ara Sarafian">Ara Sarafian</a>, the population of Armenians should have been approximately 1,700,000 prior to the start of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[123]</a></sup> However, that number had plunged to 284,157 two years later in 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Justin_McCarthy_(American_historian)" title="Justin McCarthy (American historian)">Justin McCarthy</a> calculated an estimate of the pre-war Armenian population, then subtracted his estimate of survivors, arriving at a figure of a little less than 600,000 for Armenian casualties for the period 1914 to 1922.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[125]</a></sup> In a more recent essay, he projected that if the Armenian records of 1913 were accurate, 250,000 more deaths should be added, for a total of 850,000.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, McCarthy's numbers have been highly contested by many specialists. Some of them, like Frédéric Paulin, have severely criticized McCarthy's <a href="/wiki/Methodology" title="Methodology">methodology</a> and suggest that it is flawed.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[127]</a></sup> Hilmar Kaiser<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[128]</a></sup> another specialist has made similar claims, as have professor <a href="/wiki/Vahakn_Dadrian" title="Vahakn Dadrian">Vahakn Dadrian</a><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[129]</a></sup> and professor <a href="/wiki/Levon_Marashlian" title="Levon Marashlian">Levon Marashlian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[130]</a></sup> These critics not only question McCarthy's methodology and resulting calculations, but also his primary sources, the Ottoman censuses. They point out that there was no official census undertaken in 1912; rather the numbers quoted were based on the records of 1905 which were conducted during the reign of Sultan Hamid.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[131]</a></sup> While Ottoman censuses claimed an Armenian population of 1.2 million, <a href="/wiki/Fa%27iz_El-Ghusein" class="mw-redirect" title="Fa'iz El-Ghusein">Fa'iz El-Ghusein</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Kaimakam" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaimakam">Kaimakam</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kharpout" class="mw-redirect" title="Kharpout">Kharpout</a>) wrote that there were about 1.9 million Armenians in the Ottoman Empire,<sup id="cite_ref-ma_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ma-135">[132]</a></sup> and some modern scholars estimate over 2 million. German official <a href="/wiki/Max_Erwin_von_Scheubner-Richter" title="Max Erwin von Scheubner-Richter">Max Erwin von Scheubner-Richter</a> wrote that fewer than 100,000 Armenians survived the genocide, the rest having been exterminated (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de"><i>ausgerottet</i></span>).<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:329–30</sup></p>
<p>Mass killings continued under the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Turkey">Republic of Turkey</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Turkish%E2%80%93Armenian_War" title="Turkish–Armenian War">Turkish–Armenian War</a> <sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[134]</a></sup> 60,000 to 98,000 Armenian civilians were estimated to have been killed by the Turkish army.<sup id="cite_ref-Dad360-361_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dad360-361-138">[135]</a></sup> Some estimates put the total number of Armenians massacred in the hundreds of thousands.<sup id="cite_ref-Ak.C3.A7am_44-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ak.C3.A7am-44">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:327</sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[136]</a></sup> Dadrian characterized the massacres in the Caucasus as a "miniature genocide".<sup id="cite_ref-Dadrian_45-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dadrian-45">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:360</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reports_and_reactions">Reports and reactions</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Witnesses_and_testimonies_of_the_Armenian_Genocide" title="Witnesses and testimonies of the Armenian Genocide">Witnesses and testimonies of the Armenian Genocide</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:World_War_I-_Near_East_Relief_Workers_-_memory.loc.gov.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/World_War_I-_Near_East_Relief_Workers_-_memory.loc.gov.png/220px-World_War_I-_Near_East_Relief_Workers_-_memory.loc.gov.png" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/World_War_I-_Near_East_Relief_Workers_-_memory.loc.gov.png/330px-World_War_I-_Near_East_Relief_Workers_-_memory.loc.gov.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/World_War_I-_Near_East_Relief_Workers_-_memory.loc.gov.png/440px-World_War_I-_Near_East_Relief_Workers_-_memory.loc.gov.png 2x" data-file-width="2262" data-file-height="1398" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:World_War_I-_Near_East_Relief_Workers_-_memory.loc.gov.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Workers of the American Committee for Relief in the Near East in <a href="/wiki/Sivas" title="Sivas">Sivas</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hundreds of eyewitnesses, including the neutral United States and the Ottoman Empire's own allies, Germany and <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, recorded and documented numerous acts of state-sponsored massacres. Many foreign officials offered to intervene on behalf of the Armenians, including <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XV" title="Pope Benedict XV">Pope Benedict XV</a>, only to be turned away by <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Government_(Ottoman_Empire)" title="Imperial Government (Ottoman Empire)">Ottoman government</a> officials who claimed they were retaliating against a pro-Russian insurrection.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferguson_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferguson-27">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:177</sup> On 24 May 1915, the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Triple Entente</a> warned the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> that "In view of these new crimes of Turkey against humanity and civilization, the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allied Governments</a> announce publicly to the Sublime Porte that they will hold personally responsible for these crimes all members of the Ottoman Government, as well as those of their agents who are implicated in such massacres".<sup id="cite_ref-H.RES.316_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H.RES.316-140">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_U.S._Mission_in_the_Ottoman_Empire">The U.S. Mission in the Ottoman Empire</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AmbassadorMorgenthautelegram.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/AmbassadorMorgenthautelegram.jpg/220px-AmbassadorMorgenthautelegram.jpg" width="220" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/AmbassadorMorgenthautelegram.jpg/330px-AmbassadorMorgenthautelegram.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/AmbassadorMorgenthautelegram.jpg/440px-AmbassadorMorgenthautelegram.jpg 2x" data-file-width="597" data-file-height="685" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AmbassadorMorgenthautelegram.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Telegram sent by Ambassador <a href="/wiki/Henry_Morgenthau,_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Morgenthau, Sr.">Henry Morgenthau, Sr.</a> to the <a href="/wiki/State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="State Department">State Department</a> on 16 July 1915 describing the killings of Armenians as "a campaign of race extermination".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The United States had consulates throughout the Ottoman Empire, including locations in <a href="/wiki/Edirne" title="Edirne">Edirne</a>, <a href="/wiki/El%C3%A2z%C4%B1%C4%9F" class="mw-redirect" title="Elâzığ">Elâzığ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samsun" title="Samsun">Samsun</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmir" title="İzmir">İzmir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trabzon" title="Trabzon">Trebizond</a>, Van, <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Constantinople</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aleppo" title="Aleppo">Aleppo</a>. It was officially a neutral party until it joined the Allies in April 1917. In addition to the consulates, there were numerous American <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionary</a> compounds established in Armenian-populated regions, including Van and Kharput. The atrocities were reported regularly in newspapers and literary journals around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Balakian_42-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Balakian-42">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:282–5</sup></p>
<p>On his return home in 1924 after thirty years as a U.S. Consul in the Near East, and most of the preceding decade as Consul General at Smyrna, <a href="/wiki/George_Horton" title="George Horton">George Horton</a> wrote his own "account of the Systematic Extermination of Christian Populations by Mohammedans and of the Culpability of Certain Great Powers; with a True Story of the Burning of Smyrna" (1926 subtitle, <i>The Blight of Asia</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Horton_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horton-141">[138]</a></sup> Horton's account quoted numerous contemporary communications and eyewitness reports including one of the <a href="/wiki/Massacre_of_Phocaea" title="Massacre of Phocaea">massacre of Phocea</a> in 1914, by a Frenchman, and two of the Armenian massacres of 1914/15, by an American citizen and a German missionary.<sup id="cite_ref-Horton_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horton-141">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:28–29, 34–37.</sup> It also quoted U.S. businessman <a href="/wiki/Walter_M._Geddes" title="Walter M. Geddes">Walter M. Geddes</a> regarding his time in Damascus: "several Turks[,] whom I interviewed, told me that the motive of this exile was to exterminate the race."<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many Americans spoke out against the genocide, including former president <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabbi" title="Rabbi">rabbi</a> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Wise" class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen Wise">Stephen Wise</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alice_Stone_Blackwell" title="Alice Stone Blackwell">Alice Stone Blackwell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/William_Jennings_Bryan" title="William Jennings Bryan">William Jennings Bryan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Secretary_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Secretary of State">U.S. Secretary of State</a> to June 1915. In the U.S. and the United Kingdom, children were regularly reminded to clean their plates while eating and to "remember the starving Armenians".<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ambassador_Morgenthau.27s_Story">Ambassador Morgenthau's Story</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Morgen23.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Morgen23.gif/220px-Morgen23.gif" width="220" height="328" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Morgen23.gif/330px-Morgen23.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Morgen23.gif/440px-Morgen23.gif 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="745" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Morgen23.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Report from a German missionary on the massacre of Armenians from Erzerum, 31 July 1915</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ambassador_Morgenthau%27s_Story" title="Ambassador Morgenthau's Story">Ambassador Morgenthau's Story</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="2996.1142857143" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Morgenthausstorychapter24.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons">
<source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b6/Morgenthausstorychapter24.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (79 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="78888" /></audio></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Morgenthausstorychapter24.ogg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Audio recording of Chapter 24, "The Murder of a Nation", from <i>Ambassador Morgenthau's Story</i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As the orders for deportations and massacres were enacted, many consular officials reported what they were witnessing to Ambassador <a href="/wiki/Henry_Morgenthau,_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Morgenthau, Sr.">Henry Morgenthau, Sr.</a>, who described the massacres as a "campaign of race extermination" in a telegram sent to the <a href="/wiki/State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="State Department">State Department</a> on 16 July 1915. In memoirs that he completed during 1918, Morgenthau wrote, "When the Turkish authorities gave the orders for these deportations, they were merely giving the death warrant to a whole race; they understood this well, and, in their conversations with me, they made no particular attempt to conceal the fact&#160;..."<sup id="cite_ref-Morgenthau_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morgenthau-57">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:213</sup> The memoirs and reports vividly described the methods used by Ottoman forces and documented numerous instances of atrocities committed against the Christian minority.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Allied_forces_in_the_Middle_East">Allied forces in the Middle East</span></h3>
<p>On the Middle Eastern front, the British military was engaged fighting the Ottoman forces in southern Syria and <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>. British diplomat <a href="/wiki/Gertrude_Bell" title="Gertrude Bell">Gertrude Bell</a> filed the following report after hearing the account from a captured Ottoman soldier:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The battalion left Aleppo on 3 February and reached Ras al-Ain in twelve hours&#160;... some 12,000 Armenians were concentrated under the guardianship of some hundred <a href="/wiki/Kurds" title="Kurds">Kurds</a>&#160;... These Kurds were called gendarmes, but in reality mere butchers; bands of them were publicly ordered to take parties of Armenians, of both sexes, to various destinations, but had secret instructions to destroy the males, children and old women&#160;... One of these gendarmes confessed to killing 100 Armenian men himself&#160;... the empty desert cisterns and caves were also filled with corpses&#160;...<sup id="cite_ref-Fisk_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fisk-65">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:327</sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> described the massacres as an "administrative holocaust" and noted that "the clearance of the race from Asia Minor was about as complete as such an act, on a scale so great, could well be.&#160;... There is no reasonable doubt that this crime was planned and executed for political reasons. The opportunity presented itself for clearing Turkish soil of a Christian race opposed to all Turkish ambitions, cherishing national ambitions that could only be satisfied at the expense of Turkey, and planted geographically between Turkish and Caucasian Moslems".<sup id="cite_ref-Fisk_65-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fisk-65">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:329</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Arnold_Toynbee:_The_Treatment_of_Armenians">Arnold Toynbee: <i>The Treatment of Armenians</i></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Treatment_of_Armenians_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="The Treatment of Armenians in the Ottoman Empire">The Treatment of Armenians in the Ottoman Empire</a></div>
<p>Historian <a href="/wiki/Arnold_J._Toynbee" title="Arnold J. Toynbee">Arnold J. Toynbee</a> published the collection of documents <i><a href="/wiki/The_Treatment_of_Armenians_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="The Treatment of Armenians in the Ottoman Empire">The Treatment of Armenians in the Ottoman Empire</a></i> in 1916. Together with British politician and historian <a href="/wiki/James_Bryce,_1st_Viscount_Bryce" title="James Bryce, 1st Viscount Bryce">Viscount James Bryce</a>, he compiled statements from survivors and eyewitnesses from other countries including Germany, Italy, the Netherlands, Sweden, and Switzerland, who similarly attested to the systematic massacre of innocent Armenians by Ottoman government forces.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bryce had submitted the work to scholars for verification before its publication. <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a> Regius Professor <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Murray" title="Gilbert Murray">Gilbert Murray</a> stated, "...&#160;the evidence of these letters and reports will bear any scrutiny and overpower any skepticism. Their genuineness is established beyond question".<sup id="cite_ref-Dadrian_45-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dadrian-45">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:228</sup> Other professors, including <a href="/wiki/H._A._L._Fisher" title="H. A. L. Fisher">Herbert Fisher</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield University">Sheffield University</a> and former <a href="/wiki/American_Bar_Association" title="American Bar Association">American Bar Association</a> president <a href="/wiki/Moorfield_Storey" title="Moorfield Storey">Moorfield Storey</a>, came to the same conclusion.<sup id="cite_ref-Dadrian_45-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dadrian-45">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:228–29</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Austrian_and_German_joint_mission">Austrian and German joint mission</span></h3>
<p>As allies during the war, the Imperial German mission in the Ottoman Empire included both military and civilian components. Germany had brokered a deal with the <a href="/wiki/Sublime_Porte" title="Sublime Porte">Sublime Porte</a> to commission the building of a railroad called the <a href="/wiki/Baghdad_Railway" title="Baghdad Railway">Baghdad Railway</a> that would stretch from Berlin to the Middle East. At the beginning of 1915, Germany's diplomatic mission was led by Ambassador <a href="/wiki/Hans_Freiherr_von_Wangenheim" title="Hans Freiherr von Wangenheim">Hans Freiherr von Wangenheim</a> who, upon his death in 1915, was succeeded by Count <a href="/wiki/Paul_Wolff_Metternich" title="Paul Wolff Metternich">Paul Wolff Metternich</a>. Like Morgenthau, von Wangenheim began receiving many disturbing messages from consular officials around the Ottoman Empire that detailed the massacres of Armenians. From the province of <a href="/wiki/Adana" title="Adana">Adana</a>, Consul Eugene Buge reported that the CUP chief had sworn to massacre any Armenians who had survived the deportation marches.<sup id="cite_ref-Balakian_42-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Balakian-42">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:186</sup> In June 1915, von Wangenheim sent a cable to Berlin reporting that Talaat had admitted that the deportations were not "being carried out because of 'military considerations alone'". One month later, he came to the conclusion that there "no longer was doubt that the Porte was trying to exterminate the Armenian race in the Turkish Empire".<sup id="cite_ref-Fromkin_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fromkin-66">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:213</sup></p>
<p>When Wolff-Metternich succeeded von Wangenheim, he continued to dispatch similar cables: "The Committee [CUP] demands the extirpation of the last remnants of the Armenians and the government must yield&#160;... A Committee representative is assigned to each of the provincial administrations&#160;... <a href="/wiki/Turkification" title="Turkification">Turkification</a> means license to expel, to kill or destroy everything that is not Turkish".<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another notable figure in the German military camp was <a href="/wiki/Max_Erwin_von_Scheubner-Richter" title="Max Erwin von Scheubner-Richter">Max Erwin von Scheubner-Richter</a>, who documented various massacres of Armenians. He sent fifteen reports regarding "deportations and mass killings" to the German chancellery. His final report noted that fewer than 100,000 Armenians were left alive in the Ottoman Empire: the rest having been exterminated (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de"><i>ausgerottet</i></span>).<sup id="cite_ref-Fisk_65-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fisk-65">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:329–30</sup> Scheubner-Richter also detailed the methods of the Ottoman government, noting its use of the Special Organization and other bureaucratized instruments of genocide, as well as how the Ottomans would provoke and exaggerate Armenian self-defense in order to create the illusion of a rebellion. This was to give justification for the deportation of Armenians, which is still argued by genocide deniers to this day. Richter admits the deportations were intentionally meant to cover up the slaughter of Armenians:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>I have conducted a series of conversations with competent and influential Turkish personages, and these are my impressions: A large segment of the Ittihadist [Young Turk] party maintains the viewpoint that the Turkish empire should be based only on the principle of Islam and Pan-Turkism. Its non-Muslim and non-Turkish inhabitants should either be forcibly islamized, or otherwise they ought to be destroyed. These gentlemen believe that the time is propitious for the realization of this plan. The first item on this agenda concerns the liquidation of the Armenians. Ittihad will dangle before the Allies a specter of an alleged revolution prepared by the Armenian Dashnak party. Moreover, local incidents of social unrest and acts of Armenian self defense will deliberately be provoked and inflated and will be used as pretexts to effect the deportations. Once en route, however, the convoys will be attacked and exterminated by Kurdish and Turkish brigands, and in part by gendarmes, who will be instigated for that purpose by Ittihad.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[144]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>According to Bat Ye'or, an Israeli historian, the Germans also witnessed Armenians being burned to death. She writes: "The Germans, allies of the Turks in the First World War ... saw how civil populations were shut up in churches and burned, or gathered en masse in camps, tortured to death, and reduced to ashes".<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[145]</a></sup> German officers stationed in eastern Turkey disputed the government's assertion that Armenian revolts had broken out, suggesting that the areas were "quiet until the deportations began".<sup id="cite_ref-Fromkin_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fromkin-66">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:212</sup> Other Germans openly supported the Ottoman policy against the Armenians. As <a href="/wiki/Hans_Humann" title="Hans Humann">Hans Humann</a>, the German naval attaché in Constantinople said to US Ambassador <a href="/wiki/Henry_Morgenthau,_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Morgenthau, Sr.">Henry Morgenthau</a>:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>I have lived in Turkey the larger part of my life&#160;... and I know the Armenians. I also know that both Armenians and Turks cannot live together in this country. One of these races has got to go. And I don't blame the Turks for what they are doing to the Armenians. I think that they are entirely justified. The weaker nation must succumb. The Armenians desire to dismember Turkey; they are against the Turks and the Germans in this war, and they therefore have no right to exist here.<sup id="cite_ref-Morgenthau_57-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morgenthau-57">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:257</sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In a genocide conference held in 2001, professor Wolfgang Wipperman of the <a href="/wiki/Free_University_of_Berlin" title="Free University of Berlin">Free University of Berlin</a> introduced documents evidencing that the German High Command was aware of the mass killings at the time but chose not to interfere or speak out.<sup id="cite_ref-Fisk_65-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fisk-65">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:331</sup> In his reports to Berlin in 1917, General <a href="/wiki/Hans_von_Seeckt" title="Hans von Seeckt">Hans von Seeckt</a> supported the reforming efforts of the Young Turks, writing that "the inner weakness of Turkey in their entirety, call for the history and custom of the new Turkish empire to be written".<sup id="cite_ref-Dabag_pages_113-135_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dabag_pages_113-135-149">[146]</a></sup> Seeckt added that "Only a few moments of the destruction are still mentioned. The upper levels of society had become unwarlike, the main reason being the increasing mixing with foreign elements of a long standing unculture".<sup id="cite_ref-Dabag_pages_113-135_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dabag_pages_113-135-149">[146]</a></sup> Seeckt blamed all of the problems of the Ottoman Empire on the Jews and the Armenians, whom he portrayed as a fifth column working for the Allies.<sup id="cite_ref-Dabag_pages_113-135_149-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dabag_pages_113-135-149">[146]</a></sup> In July 1918, Seeckt sent a message to Berlin stating that "It is an impossible state of affairs to be allied with the Turks and to stand up for the Armenians. In my view any consideration, Christian, sentimental, and political should be eclipsed by a hard, but clear necessity for war".<sup id="cite_ref-Dabag_pages_113-135_149-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dabag_pages_113-135-149">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>One photograph shows two unidentified German army officers, in company of three Turkish soldiers and a Kurdish man, standing amidst human remains. The discovery of this photograph prompted English journalist <a href="/wiki/Robert_Fisk" title="Robert Fisk">Robert Fisk</a> to draw a direct line from the Armenian Genocide to the Holocaust. Fisk, while acknowledging the role playing by most German diplomats and parliamentaries in the condemnation of the Ottoman Turks, noted that some of the German witnesses to the Armenian holocaust would later go on to play a role in the Nazi regime. For example, <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Freiherr_von_Neurath" class="mw-redirect" title="Konstantin Freiherr von Neurath">Konstantin Freiherr von Neurath</a>, who was attached to the Turkish 4th Army in 1915 with instructions to monitor "operations" against the Armenians, later became Hitler's foreign minister and "Protector of Bohemia and Moravia" during <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Heydrich" title="Reinhard Heydrich">Reinhard Heydrich</a>'s terror in Czechoslovakia.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[147]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Armin_T._Wegner">Armin T. Wegner</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Armin_T._Wegner" title="Armin T. Wegner">Armin T. Wegner</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Armintwegner1890s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Armintwegner1890s.jpg/220px-Armintwegner1890s.jpg" width="220" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Armintwegner1890s.jpg/330px-Armintwegner1890s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Armintwegner1890s.jpg/440px-Armintwegner1890s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1413" data-file-height="1783" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Armintwegner1890s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Armin T. Wegner</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>German aspiring writer <a href="/wiki/Armin_T._Wegner" title="Armin T. Wegner">Armin T. Wegner</a> enrolled as a medic during the winter of 1914–15. He defied censorship by taking hundreds of photographs<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[148]</a></sup> of Armenians being deported and subsequently starving in northern Syrian camps<sup id="cite_ref-Fisk_65-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fisk-65">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:326</sup> and in the deserts of Deir-er-Zor. Wegner was part of a German detachment under field marshal <a href="/wiki/Colmar_Freiherr_von_der_Goltz" title="Colmar Freiherr von der Goltz">von der Goltz</a> stationed near the <a href="/wiki/Baghdad_Railway" title="Baghdad Railway">Baghdad Railway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>. He later stated: "I venture to claim the right of setting before you these pictures of misery and terror which passed before my eyes during nearly two years, and which will never be obliterated from my mind.".<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[149]</a></sup> He was eventually arrested by the Germans and recalled to Germany.</p>
<p>Wegner protested against the atrocities in an open letter submitted to U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a> at the peace conference of 1919. The letter made a case for the creation of an independent Armenian state. Also in 1919, he published <i>The Road of No Return</i> ("Der Weg ohne Heimkehr"), a collection of letters he had written during what he deemed the "martyrdom" (German: "Martyrium") of the Armenians.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[150]</a></sup> A documentary film depicting Wegner's personal account of the Armenian Genocide through his own photographs, called "Destination Nowhere: The Witness" and produced by Dr J. Michael Hagopian, premiered in Fresno on 25 April 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[151]</a></sup> Prior to the release of the documentary, he was honored at the Armenian Genocide Museum in Yerevan for championing the plight of Armenians throughout his life.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_Empire_and_Turkey">Ottoman Empire and Turkey</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mehmed_Celal_Bey.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Mehmed_Celal_Bey.jpg/170px-Mehmed_Celal_Bey.jpg" width="170" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7e/Mehmed_Celal_Bey.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="230" data-file-height="280" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mehmed_Celal_Bey.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aleppo Governor <a href="/wiki/Mehmet_Celal_Bey" title="Mehmet Celal Bey">Mehmet Celal Bey</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although many documents related to systematic massacres were destroyed during and after the genocide,<sup id="cite_ref-bartrop_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bartrop-155">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vahakn1_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vahakn1-156">[153]</a></sup> Turkish historian Taner Akçam states that the "Turkish sources we already possess provide sufficient information to prove that what befell the Armenians in 1915 was a Genocide."<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[154]</a></sup> Historian Ara Sarafian similarly notes that "the available Ottoman materials, especially when used alongside alternative sources (such as United States records or Armenian survivor accounts), support the Armenian Genocide thesis."<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alongside official documentation, many Turkish public figures during the time have acknowledged the systematic nature of the massacres. Historian <a href="/wiki/Ahmet_Refik_Alt%C4%B1nay" title="Ahmet Refik Altınay">Ahmet Refik (Altınay)</a> wrote in 1919: "The <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Union_and_Progress" title="Committee of Union and Progress">Unionists</a> (Committee of Union and Progress) wanted to remove the problem of <a href="/wiki/Vil%C3%A2y%C3%A2t-%C4%B1_Sitte" class="mw-redirect" title="Vilâyât-ı Sitte">Vilâyât-ı Sitte</a> by annihilating Armenians."<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[156]</a></sup> Turkish novelist <a href="/wiki/Halide_Edip" class="mw-redirect" title="Halide Edip">Halide Edip</a>, who was openly critical of the decisions made by the Ottoman government towards the Armenians, wrote in <i>Vakit</i> on 21 October 1918: "We slaughtered the innocent Armenian population...We tried to extinguish the Armenians through methods that belong to the medieval times".<sup id="cite_ref-insel_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insel-160">[157]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[158]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Abd%C3%BClmecid_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdülmecid II">Abdülmecid II</a>, the last <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Caliphate" title="Ottoman Caliphate">Caliph of Islam</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Dynasty">Ottoman Dynasty</a>, said of the policy: "I refer to those awful massacres. They are the greatest stain that has ever disgraced our nation and race. They were entirely the work of Talat and Enver.".<sup id="cite_ref-najmuddin_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-najmuddin-162">[159]</a></sup> Senator Ahmet Riza stated: "Let's face it, we Turks savagely killed off the Armenians."<sup id="cite_ref-robertfisk_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-robertfisk-163">[160]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[161]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[162]</a></sup> Grand Vizier <a href="/wiki/Damad_Ferid_Pasha" class="mw-redirect" title="Damad Ferid Pasha">Damad Ferid Pasha</a>, speaking about the Armenians in the New York Times (26 June 1919), said: "The whole civilised world was shocked by the recital of the crimes alleged to have been committed by the Turks. It is far from my thought to cast a veil over these misdeeds, which are such as to make the conscience of mankind shudder with horror for ever; still less will I endeavour to minimise the degree of guilt of the actors in the great drama. The aim which I have set myself is that of showing to the world with proofs in my hand, who are the truly responsible authors of these terrible crimes."<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[163]</a></sup> Interior Minister <a href="/wiki/Ali_Kemal_Bey" class="mw-redirect" title="Ali Kemal Bey">Ali Kemal Bey</a> wrote in <i>Alemdar</i> on 18 July 1919: "Don't let us try to throw the blame on the Armenians; we must not flatter ourselves that the world is filled with idiots. We have plundered the possessions of the men whom we deported and massacred; we have sanctioned theft in our Chamber and our Senate."<sup id="cite_ref-vahakn1_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vahakn1-156">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-najmuddin_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-najmuddin-162">[159]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Re%C5%9Fid_Akif_Pa%C5%9Fa" class="mw-redirect" title="Reşid Akif Paşa">Reşid Akif Paşa</a>, Vali of Sivas and head of the Council of State, is especially known for providing important testimony during the Ottoman Parliament session of 21 November 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-Ak.C3.A7am_44-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ak.C3.A7am-44">[41]</a></sup> His speech outlined the process of how the official order of deportation contained vague terminology only to be clarified by special orders of "massacres" sent directly from the Committee of Union and Progress headquarters and oftentimes the residence of Talat Pasha himself:<sup id="cite_ref-Dadrian_45-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dadrian-45">[42]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>During my few days of service in this government I've learned of a few secrets and have come across something interesting. The deportation order was issued through official channels by the minister of the interior and sent to the provinces. Following this order the [CUP] Central Committee circulated its own ominous order to all parties to allow the gangs to carry out their wretched task. Thus the gangs were in the field, ready for their atrocious slaughter.</p>
</blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Turkish_statesman_denounces_atrocities.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Turkish_statesman_denounces_atrocities.png/220px-Turkish_statesman_denounces_atrocities.png" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Turkish_statesman_denounces_atrocities.png/330px-Turkish_statesman_denounces_atrocities.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/ba/Turkish_statesman_denounces_atrocities.png 2x" data-file-width="438" data-file-height="251" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Turkish_statesman_denounces_atrocities.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/%C5%9Eerif_Pasha" title="Şerif Pasha">Mehmed Şerif Pasha</a> was a former member of the Young Turk government who denounced the annihilation (The New York Times, 10 October 1915).<sup id="cite_ref-newyorktimes_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newyorktimes-167">[164]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Some politicians tried to prevent the deportations and subsequent massacres. One such politician, <a href="/wiki/Mehmet_Celal_Bey" title="Mehmet Celal Bey">Mehmet Celal Bey</a>, was known for saving thousands of lives and often called the Turkish <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Schindler" class="mw-redirect" title="Oscar Schindler">Oscar Schindler</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[165]</a></sup> During his time as governor of Aleppo, Celal Bey did not believe that the deportations were meant to "annihilate" the Armenians: "I admit, I did not believe that these orders, these actions revolved around the annihilation of the Armenians. I never imagined that any government could take upon itself to annihilate its own citizens in this manner, in effect destroying its human capital, which must be seen as the country's greatest treasure. I presumed that the actions being carried out were measures deriving from a desire to temporarily remove the Armenians from the theater of war and taken as the result of wartime exigencies."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAk.C3.A7am2012425_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAk.C3.A7am2012425-169">[166]</a></sup> However, he later admitted that he was mistaken and that the goal was "to attempt to annihilate" the Armenians.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAk.C3.A7am2012425_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAk.C3.A7am2012425-169">[166]</a></sup> When defying the orders of deportation, Celal Bey was removed from his post as governor of Aleppo and transferred to Konya.<sup id="cite_ref-Ak.C3.A7am_44-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ak.C3.A7am-44">[41]</a></sup> However, as the deportations continued, he repeatedly demanded that the central authorities provide shelter for the deportees.<sup id="cite_ref-derogy_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-derogy-170">[167]</a></sup> In addition to these demands, he sent the Sublime Porte many telegrams and letters of protest stating that the "measures taken against the Armenians were, from every point of view, contrary to the higher interests of the fatherland."<sup id="cite_ref-derogy_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-derogy-170">[167]</a></sup> His demands, however, were ignored.<sup id="cite_ref-derogy_170-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-derogy-170">[167]</a></sup> Celal Bey said: "Blood flowed instead of water in the river, and thousands of innocent children, blameless elderly, helpless women and strong youths were flowing towards death in this blood flow."<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[168]</a></sup> Hasan Mazhar Bey, who was appointed Vali of Ankara on 18 June 1914, is also known for having refused to proceed with the order of deportations.<sup id="cite_ref-bedrosyanweekly_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bedrosyanweekly-172">[169]</a></sup> Due to his refusal to deport the Armenians, Mazhar Bey was removed from his post as governor in August 1915 and replaced with Atif Bey, a prominent member of the Special Organization.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[170]</a></sup> He recalled: "Then one day Atif Bey came to me and orally conveyed the interior minister's orders that the Armenians were to be murdered during the deportation. 'No, Atif Bey,' I said, 'I am a governor, not a bandit, I cannot do this, I will leave this post and you can come and do it.'"<sup id="cite_ref-Ak.C3.A7am_44-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ak.C3.A7am-44">[41]</a></sup> After leaving his post, Mazhar went on to report that "in the <a href="/wiki/Kaza" title="Kaza">kaza</a> [district], the plunder of Armenian property, by both officials and the population, assumed incredible proportions."<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[171]</a></sup> He also became the key figure in the establishment of the Mazhar Commission, an investigative committee which immediately took up the task of gathering evidence and testimonies, with a special effort to obtain inquiries on civil servants implicated in massacres committed against Armenians.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[172]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCleyman_Nazif" title="Süleyman Nazif">Süleyman Nazif</a>, the Vali of Baghdad, who but later resigned in protest of the Ottoman government's policy towards the Armenians, wrote in a 28 November 1918 issue of the <i>Hadisat</i> newspaper: "Under the guise of deportations, mass murder was perpetrated. Given the fact that the crime is all too evident, the perpetrators should have been hanged already."<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the Republican period, several Turkish politicians expressed their discontent with the deportations and subsequent massacres. <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal Atatürk">Mustafa Kemal Atatürk</a>, the first President and founder of the Republic of Turkey, consistently used the term "shameful act" (Turkish: <i>fazahat</i>) when referring to the massacres.<sup id="cite_ref-vahakn1_156-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vahakn1-156">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ottowa_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ottowa-178">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[176]</a></sup> In the 1 August 1926 issue of the <i>Los Angeles Examiner</i>, Atatürk also said that the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turk" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Turk">Young Turk</a> Party was responsible for "... millions of our Christian subjects who were ruthlessly driven en masse from their homes and massacred".<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[177]</a></sup> At a secret session of the National Assembly, held on 17 October 1920, <a href="/wiki/Hasan_Fehmi_(Ata%C3%A7)" title="Hasan Fehmi (Ataç)">Hasan Fehmi (Ataç)</a>, deputy of Gümüşhane, said: "As you know, the issue of relocation was an event that made the world to yell blue and made all of us to be considered murderers. We knew, before we did it, that the Christian world would not tolerate it and they would direct their anger and hatred toward us. Why did we impute the title of murderer to our race? Why did we enter into such decisive and difficult struggle? That was done just to secure the future of our country, which we know to be more precious and sacred than our lives."<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[178]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_military">Russian military</span></h3>
<p>The Russian Empire's response to the bombardment of its Black Sea naval ports was primarily a land campaign through the Caucasus. Early victories against the Ottoman Empire from the winter of 1914 to the spring 1915 saw significant gains of territory, including relieving the Armenian bastion resisting in the city of Van in May 1915. The Russians also reported encountering the bodies of unarmed civilian Armenians as they advanced.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[179]</a></sup> In March 1916, the scenes they saw in the city of <a href="/wiki/Erzurum" title="Erzurum">Erzurum</a> led the Russians to retaliate against the Ottoman III Army whom they held responsible for the massacres, destroying it in its entirety.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[180]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scandinavian_missionaries_and_diplomats">Scandinavian missionaries and diplomats</span></h3>
<p>Although a neutral state throughout the war, Sweden had permanent representatives in the Ottoman Empire who closely followed and continuously reported on major developments there. Its embassy in Constantinople was led by Ambassador <a href="/wiki/Cossva_Anckarsv%C3%A4rd" title="Cossva Anckarsvärd">Cossva Anckarsvärd</a>, with M. Ahlgren as envoy and Captain <a href="/wiki/Einar_af_Wirs%C3%A9n" title="Einar af Wirsén">Einar af Wirsén</a> as military attaché. On 7 July 1915, Ambassador Anckarsvärd dispatched a two-page report concerning the Armenian massacres to <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>. The report began as follows:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The persecutions of the Armenians have reached hair-raising proportions and all points to the fact that the Young Turks want to seize the opportunity, since due to different reasons there are no effective external pressure to be feared, to once and for all put an end to the Armenian question. The means for this are quite simple and consist of the extermination (utrotandet) of the Armenian nation.<sup id="cite_ref-Avedian_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avedian-184">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:39</sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>On 9 August 1915, Anckarsvärd dispatched yet another report, confirming his suspicions regarding the plans of the Turkish government, "It is obvious that the Turks are taking the opportunity to, now during the war, annihilate [utplåna] the Armenian nation so that when the peace comes no Armenian question longer exists".<sup id="cite_ref-Avedian_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avedian-184">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:41</sup></p>
<p>Reflecting upon the situation in Turkey during the final stages of the war, Envoy Alhgren presented an analysis of the prevailing situation in Turkey and the hard times which had befallen the population. In explaining the increased living costs he identified a number of reasons: "obstacles for domestic trade, the almost total paralysing of the foreign trade and finally the strong decreasing of labour power, caused partly by the mobilisation but partly also by the extermination of the Armenian race [utrotandet af den armeniska rasen]".<sup id="cite_ref-Avedian_184-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avedian-184">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:52</sup></p>
<p>Wirsén, when writing his memoirs from his mission to the Balkans and Turkey, <i>Minnen från fred och krig</i> ("Memories from Peace and War"), dedicated an entire chapter to the Armenian genocide, entitled <i>Mordet på en nation</i> ("The Murder of a Nation"). Commenting on the interpretation that the deportations resulted from the purported collaboration of the Armenians with the Russians, Wirsen states that the deportations were nothing but a cover for their extermination: "Officially, these had the goal to move the entire Armenian population to the steppe regions of Northern Mesopotamia and Syria, but in reality they aimed to exterminate [utrota] the Armenians, whereby the pure Turkish element in Asia Minor would achieve a dominating position".<sup id="cite_ref-Avedian_184-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avedian-184">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:28</sup> He concluded: "The annihilation of the Armenian nation in Asia Minor must revolt all human feelings&#160;... The way the Armenian problem was solved was hair-raising. I can still see in front of me Talaat's cynical expression, when he emphasized that the Armenian question was solved".<sup id="cite_ref-Avedian_184-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avedian-184">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:29</sup></p>
<p>Norwegian missionary nurse <a href="/wiki/Bodil_Katharine_Bi%C3%B8rn" title="Bodil Katharine Biørn">Bodil Biørn</a> was based in the town of Mezereh (now Elazig) and later in Mush, where she worked for widows and orphaned children in cooperation with other missionaries. She witnessed the massacres in Mush and saw most of the children in her care murdered along with Armenian priests, teachers, and assistants. She escaped after nine days on horseback but stayed on in the region for another two years under increasingly difficult working conditions. After a period at home she again went to Armenia and, until she retired in 1935, worked for Armenian refugees in Syria and Lebanon. Bodil Biørn was also an able photographer. Many of her photos are now in the National Archives of Norway. In combination with her comments, written in her photo albums or on the back of the prints themselves, these photos bear strong witness of the atrocities that she saw.<sup id="cite_ref-NorwegianStateArchive_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwegianStateArchive-185">[182]</a></sup></p>
