<p>Danish missionary <a href="/wiki/Maria_Jacobsen" title="Maria Jacobsen">Maria Jacobsen</a> wrote her experiences in a diary entitled <i>Diaries of a Danish Missionary: Harpoot, 1907–1919</i>, which according to genocide scholar Ara Sarafian, is a "documentation of the utmost significance" for research of the Armenian Genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-Reporter_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reporter-186">[183]</a></sup> Jacobsen would later be known for having saved thousands of Armenians through various relief efforts in the aftermath of the Armenian Genocide .<sup id="cite_ref-Reporter_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reporter-186">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nefissa_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nefissa-187">[184]</a></sup> She wrote: "It is quite obvious that the purpose of their departure is the extermination of the Armenian people."<sup id="cite_ref-nefissa_187-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nefissa-187">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-diary123_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diary123-188">[185]</a></sup> Another Danish missionary, Aage Meyer Benedictsen, wrote in regards to the massacres that it was a "shattering crime, probably the largest in the history of the world: The attempt, planned and executed in cold blood, to murder a whole people, the Armenian, during the World War."<sup id="cite_ref-MATTHIAS_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MATTHIAS-189">[186]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Johannes_%C3%98strup" title="Johannes Østrup">Johannes Østrup</a>, a Danish <a href="/wiki/Philologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Philologist">philologist</a> and professor at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Copenhagen" title="University of Copenhagen">University of Copenhagen</a>, met with several Young Turk politicians and leaders prior to the start of World War I. In his memoirs, Østrup recounts his meeting with Talat Pasha in the autumn of 1910 in which he writes that Talat talked openly about his plans to "exterminate" the Armenians.<sup id="cite_ref-danishdiplomat_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-danishdiplomat-190">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ostrup_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ostrup-191">[188]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Persia">Persia</span></h3>
<p>Due to the period of weak central government and <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>'s inability to protect its territorial integrity, no resistance was offered by the mostly Islamic Persian troops when, after the withdrawal of Russian troops from the extreme northwest of Persia, Islamic Turks invaded the town of <a href="/wiki/Salmas" title="Salmas">Salmas</a> in northwestern Persia and tortured and massacred the Christian Armenian inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[189]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mohammad-Ali_Jamalzadeh" title="Mohammad-Ali Jamalzadeh">Mohammad-Ali Jamalzadeh</a>, a prominent Persian writer in the 20th century, studied in Europe where he joined a group of Iranian nationalists in Berlin who were to eventually start a newspaper (Rastakhiz) in Baghdad in 1915. After remaining in Baghdad, Jamalzadeh went to Constantinople where he witnessed the deportations of Armenians and encountered many corpses during his journey.<sup id="cite_ref-iranica_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iranica-193">[190]</a></sup> He wrote of his experiences and eyewitness accounts decades later in two books entitled "Qatl-e Amm-e Armanian" (<a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>: <span lang="fa" dir="rtl">قتل عام ارمنیان</span>‎‎, literally; <i>Armenian massacres</i>) and "Qatl o ḡārat-e Arāmaneh dar Torkiya" (On the massacres of Armenians in Ottoman Turkey) which were published in 1972 and 1963 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-iranica_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iranica-193">[190]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Studies_on_the_Genocide">Studies on the Genocide</span></h2>
<p>The Armenian Genocide is widely corroborated by international genocide scholars. The <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Genocide_Scholars" title="International Association of Genocide Scholars">International Association of Genocide Scholars</a> (IAGS), consisting of the world's foremost experts on genocide,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[191]</a></sup> unanimously passed a formal resolution affirming the factuality of the Armenian Genocide. According to IAGS, "Every book on comparative genocide studies in the English language contains a segment on the Armenian Genocide. Leading texts in the international law of genocide such as <a href="/wiki/William_Schabas" title="William Schabas">William Schabas</a>'s <i>Genocide in International Law</i> cite the Armenian Genocide as precursor to the Holocaust and as a precedent for the law on crimes against humanity. Polish <a href="/wiki/Jurist" title="Jurist">jurist</a> Raphael Lemkin, when he coined the term <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> in 1943, cited the Turkish extermination of the Armenians and the Nazi extermination of the Jews as defining examples of what he meant by genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-aur_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aur-195">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-schab_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schab-196">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Moses2004_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moses2004-197">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ushmm_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ushmm-198">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jww_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jww-199">[196]</a></sup> The killings of Armenians is genocide as defined by the 1948 United Nations Convention on the Prevention and Punishment of the Crime of Genocide. 126 leading scholars of the holocaust including <a href="/wiki/Elie_Wiesel" title="Elie Wiesel">Elie Wiesel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yehuda_Bauer" title="Yehuda Bauer">Yehuda Bauer</a> placed a statement in the <i>New York Times</i> in June 2000 declaring the "incontestable fact of the Armenian genocide" and urging western democracies to acknowledge it. "The <a href="/wiki/Institute_on_the_Holocaust_and_Genocide" title="Institute on the Holocaust and Genocide">Institute on the Holocaust and Genocide</a> (Jerusalem), and the Institute for the Study of Genocide (NYC), have affirmed the historical fact of the Armenian Genocide".<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>Historian Stefan Ihrig observes that the Armenian Genocide was part of the prehistory of the Holocaust and that merely ten years before Hitler's rise to power the German debate on genocide, begun in 1919, concluded with justifications of genocide and calls for the expulsion of Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[198]</a></sup></p>
<p>A segment of speech given by <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> to <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a> commanders at his <a href="/wiki/Obersalzberg_Speech#The_Armenian_quote" class="mw-redirect" title="Obersalzberg Speech">Obersalzberg</a> records him asking rhetorically "Who, after all, speaks to-day of the annihilation of the Armenians?"<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[199]</a></sup> Historian <a href="/wiki/Margaret_L._Anderson" title="Margaret L. Anderson">Margaret L. Anderson</a> surmises, "we have no reason to doubt the remark is genuine, both attack and defense obscure an obvious reality" that the Armenian Genocide has achieved "iconic status... as the apex of horrors imaginable in 1939," and that Hitler used it to persuade the German military that committing genocide excited a great deal of "talk" but no serious consequences for a nation that perpetrates genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[200]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">Genocide</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">

data-height=&quot;160&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;196160&quot; data-framerate=&quot;29.97&quot;/&gt;&lt;source src=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/8/87/The_Genocide_Word_by_Raphael_Lemkin.ogv/The_Genocide_Word_by_Raphael_Lemkin.ogv.240p.webm&quot; type=&quot;video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;Small WebM (240P)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;WebM 240P&quot; data-transcodekey=&quot;240p.webm&quot; data-width=&quot;320&quot; type=&quot;video/ogg; codecs=&amp;quot;theora, vorbis&amp;quot;&quot; data-title=&quot;Small Ogg video (240P)&quot; data-shorttitle=&quot;Ogg 240P&quot; data-transcodekey=&quot;240p.ogv&quot; data-width=&quot;320&quot; data-height=&quot;240&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;389256&quot; data-framerate=&quot;60&quot;/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;"><img alt="File:The Genocide Word by Raphael Lemkin.ogv" style="width:330px;height:248px" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/The_Genocide_Word_by_Raphael_Lemkin.ogv/330px--The_Genocide_Word_by_Raphael_Lemkin.ogv.jpg" /><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/87/The_Genocide_Word_by_Raphael_Lemkin.ogv" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Genocide_Word_by_Raphael_Lemkin.ogv" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lemkin: the origin of the word "genocide", (CBS News)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Armenian Genocide happened before the coining of the term "genocide". English-language words and phrases used by contemporary accounts to characterise the event include "massacres", "atrocities", "annihilation", "holocaust", "the murder of a nation", "race extermination" and "a crime against humanity".<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p>The survivors of the genocide used a number of Armenian terms to name the event. Mouradian writes that "Yeghern (Crime/Catastrophe), or variants like Medz Yeghern (Great Crime) and Abrilian Yeghern (the April Crime)" were the terms most commonly used.<sup id="cite_ref-Mouradian_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mouradian-205">[202]</a></sup> The name "Aghed", usually translated as "Catastrophe", was, according to Beledian, the term most often used in Armenian literature to name the event.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[203]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[204]</a></sup> After the coining of the term genocide, the portmanteau word Armenocide was also used as a name for the Armenian Genocide.</p>
<p>Works that seek to deny the Armenian Genocide often attach qualifying words against the term genocide, such as "so-called", "alleged" or "disputed," or characterise it as a "controversy", or dismiss it as "Armenian allegations", "Armenian claims"<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[205]</a></sup> or "Armenian lies", or employ euphemisms to avoid the word genocide, such as calling it a "tragedy for both sides", or "the events of 1915".<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[206]</a></sup> American President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>'s use of the term Medz Yeghern when referring to the Armenian Genocide has been described "as a means of avoiding the word genocide".<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Raphael_Lemkin" title="Raphael Lemkin">Raphael Lemkin</a> coined the term "genocide" in 1943, with the fate of the Armenians in mind; he later explained that:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>...it happened so many times&#160;... It happened to the Armenians, then after the Armenians <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Hitler</a> took action.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[208]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Several international organizations have conducted studies of the atrocities, each in turn determining that the term "genocide" aptly describes "the Ottoman massacre of Armenians in 1915–16".<sup id="cite_ref-ictj_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ictj-212">[209]</a></sup> Among the organizations affirming this conclusion are the <a href="/wiki/International_Center_for_Transitional_Justice" title="International Center for Transitional Justice">International Center for Transitional Justice</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Genocide_Scholars" title="International Association of Genocide Scholars">International Association of Genocide Scholars</a>, and the United Nations' <a href="/wiki/Sub-Commission_on_Prevention_of_Discrimination_and_Protection_of_Minorities" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-Commission on Prevention of Discrimination and Protection of Minorities">Sub-Commission on Prevention of Discrimination and Protection of Minorities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ictj_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ictj-212">[209]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-armeniapediaictj_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-armeniapediaictj-213">[210]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Genocide_Scholars" title="International Association of Genocide Scholars">International Association of Genocide Scholars</a> affirmed<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[211]</a></sup> that scholarly evidence revealed the "Young Turk government of the Ottoman Empire began a systematic genocide of its Armenian citizens&#160;– an unarmed Christian minority population. More than a million Armenians were exterminated through direct killing, starvation, torture, and forced death marches". The IAGS also condemned Turkish attempts to deny the factual and moral reality of the Armenian Genocide. In 2007, the Elie Wiesel Foundation for Humanity produced a letter<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[212]</a></sup> signed by 53 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Laureate" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Laureate">Nobel Laureates</a> re-affirming the Genocide Scholars' conclusion that the 1915 killings of Armenians constituted genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[214]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_3" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="0" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Martyredarmeniasection3.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons">
<source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/23/Martyredarmeniasection3.ogg" type="audio/ogg" data-title="Original Ogg file (0 bps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" />
<source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/23/Martyredarmeniasection3.ogg/Martyredarmeniasection3.ogg.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Ogg Vorbis" data-shorttitle="Ogg Vorbis" data-transcodekey="ogg" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="0" /></audio></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Martyredarmeniasection3.ogg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Audio recording of Section 3 of Martyred Armenia, by <a href="/wiki/Fa%27iz_El-Ghusein" class="mw-redirect" title="Fa'iz El-Ghusein">Fa'iz El-Ghusein</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bat_Ye%27or" title="Bat Ye'or">Bat Ye'or</a> has suggested that "the genocide of the Armenians was a <a href="/wiki/Jihad" title="Jihad">jihad</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[215]</a></sup> Ye'or holds jihad and what she calls "<a href="/wiki/Dhimmitude" title="Dhimmitude">dhimmitude</a>" to be among the "principles and values" that led to the Armenian Genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[216]</a></sup> This perspective is challenged by Fà'iz el-Ghusein, a <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouin</a> Arab witness of the Armenian persecution, whose 1918 treatise aimed "to refute beforehand inventions and slanders against the Faith of Islam and against Moslems generally&#160;... [W]hat the Armenians have suffered is to be attributed to the Committee of Union and Progress&#160;... [I]t has been due to their nationalist fanaticism and their jealousy of the Armenians, and to these alone; the Faith of Islam is guiltless of their deeds".<sup id="cite_ref-El-Ghusein_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-El-Ghusein-220">[217]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:49</sup> Arnold Toynbee writes that "the <a href="/wiki/Young_Turks" title="Young Turks">Young Turks</a> made <a href="/wiki/Pan-Islamism" title="Pan-Islamism">Pan-Islamism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Nationalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Nationalism">Turkish Nationalism</a> work together for their ends, but the development of their policy shows the Islamic element receding and the Nationalist gaining ground".<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[218]</a></sup> Toynbee and various other sources report that many Armenians were spared death by marrying into Turkish families or converting to Islam. El-Ghusein points out that many converts were put to death, concerned that Westerners would come to regard the "extermination of the Armenians"<sup id="cite_ref-El-Ghusein_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-El-Ghusein-220">[217]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:49</sup> as "a black stain on the history of Islam, which ages will not efface".<sup id="cite_ref-El-Ghusein_220-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-El-Ghusein-220">[217]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:51</sup> In one instance, when an Islamic leader appealed to spare Armenian converts to Islam, El-Ghusein quotes a government functionary as responding that "politics have no religion", before sending the converts to their deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-El-Ghusein_220-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-El-Ghusein-220">[217]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:49</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition_of_the_Genocide">Recognition of the Genocide</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide_recognition" title="Armenian Genocide recognition">Armenian Genocide recognition</a></div>
<div style="float:right; width:300px; background:#f0f0f0; padding:0.7em; margin-left:1em; font-size:0.9em;">
<p><b>Council of Europe Parliamentary Assembly Resolution, 24 April 1998</b></p>
<p>"Today we commemorate the anniversary of what has been called the first genocide of the 20th century, and we salute the memory of the Armenian victims of this crime against humanity".<sup id="cite_ref-24.04.1998_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24.04.1998-26">[23]</a></sup></p>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nations_recognising_the_Armenian_Genocide.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Nations_recognising_the_Armenian_Genocide.svg/300px-Nations_recognising_the_Armenian_Genocide.svg.png" width="300" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Nations_recognising_the_Armenian_Genocide.svg/450px-Nations_recognising_the_Armenian_Genocide.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Nations_recognising_the_Armenian_Genocide.svg/600px-Nations_recognising_the_Armenian_Genocide.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1027" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nations_recognising_the_Armenian_Genocide.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
States which have recognized the Armenian Genocide.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Larnaca_monument.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Larnaca_monument.jpg/220px-Larnaca_monument.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Larnaca_monument.jpg/330px-Larnaca_monument.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Larnaca_monument.jpg/440px-Larnaca_monument.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1559" data-file-height="1169" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Larnaca_monument.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Armenian genocide monument in <a href="/wiki/Larnaca" title="Larnaca">Larnaca</a>, Cyprus. Cyprus was among the first countries to recognise the genocide.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As a response to continuing denial by the Turkish state, many activists from <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Diaspora" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian Diaspora">Armenian Diaspora</a> communities have pushed for formal recognition of the Armenian genocide from various governments around the world. Twenty-nine countries and forty-three&#160;U.S. states have adopted resolutions acknowledging the Armenian Genocide as a <i>bona fide</i> historical event.<sup id="cite_ref-Cohan_2005_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cohan_2005-222">[219]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[222]</a></sup> On 4 March 2010, a US congressional panel narrowly voted that the incident was indeed genocide; within minutes the Turkish government issued a statement critical of "this resolution which accuses the Turkish nation of a crime it has not committed". The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Assembly_of_America" title="Armenian Assembly of America">Armenian Assembly of America</a> (AAA) and the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_National_Committee_of_America" title="Armenian National Committee of America">Armenian National Committee of America</a> (ANCA) have as their main lobbying agenda to press Congress and the President for an increase of economic aid for Armenia and the reduction of economic and military assistance for Turkey. The efforts also include reaffirmation of a genocide by Ottoman Turkey in 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[223]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Armenian_Genocide&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Israel, the United Kingdom and United States do not recognize what happened a century ago as a "genocide".<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[224]</a></sup> Despite his previous public recognition and support of genocide bills, as well as election campaign promises to formally recognize the Armenian Genocide,<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[225]</a></sup> U.S. President Barack Obama, although repeating that his views on the issue have not changed, has abstained so far from using the term "genocide".<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[226]</a></sup> In his 24 April commemoration statements Obama has referred to the Armenian Genocide by its Armenian synonym, Medz Yeghern (spelled "Meds Yeghern" in the statements).<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[227]</a></sup> Despite a large number of direct descendants of the Armenian genocide living in Jerusalem, specifically in the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Quarter" title="Armenian Quarter">Armenian Quarter</a>, Israel still refuses to recognize the genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[228]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a> described it as the "First genocide of the XX century", causing a diplomatic row with Turkey. The <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Rome" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Rome">bishop of Rome</a> defended his pronouncement by saying it was his duty to honour the memory of the innocent men, women and children who were "senselessly" murdered by Ottoman Turks 100 years before he became Pontiff. He also called on all heads of state and international organizations to recognize "the truth of what transpired and oppose such crimes without ceding to ambiguity or compromise."<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[229]</a></sup> In a resolution, the European Parliament commended the statement pronounced by the Pope and encouraged Turkey to recognise the genocide and so pave the way for a "genuine reconciliation between the Turkish and Armenian peoples".<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[230]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 April 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Bundestag" title="Bundestag">German parliament</a> overwhelmingly adopted a resolution recognising the Genocide. Leading the debate, the <a href="/wiki/Bundestag" title="Bundestag">Bundestag</a> president <a href="/wiki/Norbert_Lammert" title="Norbert Lammert">Norbert Lammert</a> declared, "What happened in the middle of the First World War in the Ottoman Empire under the eyes of the world was a genocide."<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[231]</a></sup></p>
<p>A bill penalizing denial of the Armenian Genocide has been introduced in the Russian <a href="/wiki/State_Duma" title="State Duma">State Duma</a> in November 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[232]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_Turkey_and_the_Genocide">Republic of Turkey and the Genocide</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide_denial" title="Armenian Genocide denial">Armenian Genocide denial</a></div>
<p>According to Kemal Çiçek, the head of the Armenian Research Group at the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Historical_Society" title="Turkish Historical Society">Turkish Historical Society</a>, in Turkey there is no official thesis on the Armenian issue.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[233]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Republic of Turkey</a>'s formal stance is that the deaths of Armenians during the "relocation" or "deportation" cannot aptly be deemed "genocide", a position that has been supported with a plethora of diverging justifications: that the killings were not deliberate or systematically orchestrated; that the killings were justified because Armenians posed a Russian-sympathizing threat<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[234]</a></sup> as a cultural group; that the Armenians merely starved to death, or any of various characterizations referring to marauding "Armenian gangs".<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[235]</a></sup> Some suggestions seek to invalidate the genocide on semantic or anachronistic grounds (the word <i><a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a></i> was not coined until 1943). Turkish World War I casualty figures are often cited to mitigate the effect of the number of Armenian dead.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[236]</a></sup></p>
<p>Volkan Vural, retired ambassador of Turkey to Germany and Spain, says that the Turkish state should apologize for what happened to the Armenians during the deportations of 1915 and what happened to the Greeks during the <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Pogrom" class="mw-redirect" title="Istanbul Pogrom">Istanbul Pogrom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-VolkanVuralinterview_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VolkanVuralinterview-240">[237]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aghetinterview_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aghetinterview-241">[238]</a></sup> He also states, "I think that, the Armenian issue can be solved by politicians and not by historians. I don't believe that historical facts about this issue is not revealed. The historical facts are already known. The most important point here is that how these facts will be interpreted and will affect the future".<sup id="cite_ref-VolkanVuralinterview_240-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VolkanVuralinterview-240">[237]</a></sup></p>
<p>Turkish governmental sources have asserted that the historically demonstrated "tolerance of the Turkish people" itself renders the Armenian Genocide an impossibility.<sup id="cite_ref-generalstaff_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-generalstaff-242">[239]</a></sup> A <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Der Spiegel</a></i> article addressed this modern Turkish conception of history thus:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Would you admit to the crimes of your grandfathers, if these crimes didn't really happen?" asked ambassador Öymen. But the problem lies precisely in this question, says <a href="/wiki/Hrant_Dink" title="Hrant Dink">Hrant Dink</a>, publisher and editor-in-chief of the Istanbul-based Armenian weekly <i><a href="/wiki/Agos" title="Agos">Agos</a></i>. Turkey's bureaucratic elite have never really shed themselves of the Ottoman tradition—in the perpetrators, they see their fathers, whose honor they seek to defend. This tradition instills a sense of identity in Turkish nationalists—both from the left and the right, and it is passed on from generation to generation through the school system. This tradition also requires an antipole against which it could define itself. Since the times of the Ottoman Empire, religious minorities have been pushed into this role.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[240]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In 2005, Turkey started an "initiative to resolve Armenian allegations regarding 1915" by using archives in Turkey, Armenia and other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Turkish_invitation_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turkish_invitation-244">[241]</a></sup> Armenian president <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kocharian" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Kocharian">Robert Kocharian</a> rejected this offer by saying, "It is the responsibility of governments to develop bilateral relations and we do not have the right to delegate that responsibility to historians. That is why we have proposed and propose again that, without pre-conditions, we establish normal relations between our two countries".<sup id="cite_ref-Oskanian_Comments_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oskanian_Comments-245">[242]</a></sup> Additionally, Turkish foreign minister of the time, <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_G%C3%BCl" title="Abdullah Gül">Abdullah Gül</a>, invited the United States and other countries to contribute to such a commission by appointing scholars to "investigate this <a href="/wiki/Tragedy_(event)" title="Tragedy (event)">tragedy</a> and open ways for Turks and Armenians to come together".<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[243]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Prime_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Prime Minister">Turkish Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdoğan">Recep Tayyip Erdoğan</a> issued a circular that calls the government institutions to use the phrase "Events of 1915" (in Turkish, <i>1915 Olayları</i>) instead of the phrase "so-called Armenian genocide" (in Turkish, <i>sözde Ermeni Soykırımı</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[244]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span></h4>
<p>Efforts by the Turkish government and its agents to quash mention of the genocide have resulted in numerous scholarly, diplomatic, political and legal controversies.</p>
<p>In 1973, Turkey recalled its ambassador to France to protest the Genocide monument erected in <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a> "to the memory of the 1.5 million Armenian victims of the genocide ordered by the Turkish rulers in 1915".<sup id="cite_ref-Derogy1990_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Derogy1990-248">[245]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1973, the <a href="/wiki/Sub-Commission_on_Prevention_of_Discrimination_and_Protection_of_Minorities" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-Commission on Prevention of Discrimination and Protection of Minorities">Sub-Commission on Prevention of Discrimination and Protection of Minorities</a>, a former UN body, mandated special rapporteur Nicodème Ruhashyankiko to produce a report on the issue of genocide. Early drafts of Ruhashyankiko's report referred to the World War I era Ottoman massacre of Armenians as genocide, but that reference disappeared from his final report (1978) under pressure from Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[246]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> Foreign Ministry attempted to prevent any mention of the Armenian Genocide at an international conference on genocide held in <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> in 1982. Several reports suggested that Turkey had warned that <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Jews">Turkish Jews</a> might face "reprisals" if the conference permitted Armenian participation.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[247]</a></sup> This charge was "categorically denied" by Turkey;<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[248]</a></sup> the Israeli Foreign Ministry supported Turkey's protestation that there had been no threats against Jews, suggesting that its intervention in the genocide conference was based on considerations "vital to the Jewish nation".<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[249]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the same year, the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Turkish_Studies" title="Institute of Turkish Studies">Institute of Turkish Studies</a> in Washington, D.C. (ITS) was established by a $3 million grant from the Turkish Government. Israel Charny identifies the ITS and some of its foremost deniers of the Armenian genocide, such as <a href="/wiki/Stanford_J._Shaw" title="Stanford J. Shaw">Stanford Shaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heath_W._Lowry" title="Heath W. Lowry">Heath W. Lowry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Justin_McCarthy_(American_historian)" title="Justin McCarthy (American historian)">Justin McCarthy</a>, as the Turkish government's principal agency in the USA for promoting research on Turkey and the Ottoman Empire, but also denial of the Armenian Genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[250]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 1989 U.S. Senate proposal to recognize the Armenian Genocide stoked the ire of Turkey. The proposal occurred in the context of the publication of "The Slaughterhouse Province," the eyewitness report by <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Davis" title="Leslie Davis">Leslie Davis</a>, American diplomat and consul in Kharpert from 1914-1917, who reported that "thousands and thousands of Armenians, mostly innocent and helpless women and children, were butchered" in the last days of the Ottoman Empire. Turkey responded by blocking <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> visits to Turkey and suspending some US military training facilities on Turkish territory. The American scholar who assembled the US archive documents for publication, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Susan_K._Blair&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Susan K. Blair (page does not exist)">Susan K. Blair</a>, went into hiding after a series of anonymous threats.<sup id="cite_ref-nyttsp_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyttsp-254">[251]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1990, psychologist <a href="/wiki/Robert_Jay_Lifton" title="Robert Jay Lifton">Robert Jay Lifton</a> received a letter from the Turkish Ambassador to the United States, Nuzhet Kandemir, questioning his inclusion of references to the Armenian Genocide in one of his books. The ambassador inadvertently included a draft of the letter, written by scholar <a href="/wiki/Heath_W._Lowry" title="Heath W. Lowry">Heath W. Lowry</a>, advising the ambassador on how to prevent mention of the Armenian Genocide in scholarly works.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[252]</a></sup> In 1996, Lowry was named to a chair at <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a> that had been financed by the Turkish government, sparking a debate on ethics in scholarship.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith1995_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith1995-256">[253]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[254]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1993, <a href="/wiki/Rag%C4%B1p_Zarakolu" title="Ragıp Zarakolu">Ragıp Zarakolu</a>, a Turkish human rights activist, published the Turkish translation of the book called <i>History of the Genocide</i> written by <a href="/wiki/Yves_Ternon" title="Yves Ternon">Yves Ternon</a>. The book was the first to be published in Turkey that openly acknowledged the events of 1915 as <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>. Soon after its publication, he received threats and in 1994, the publishing firm of Ragıp Zorakolu was the target of a bomb attack.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[255]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prosecutors acting on their own initiative have used <a href="/wiki/Article_301_(Turkish_penal_code)" class="mw-redirect" title="Article 301 (Turkish penal code)">Article 301</a> of the Turkish Penal Code prohibiting "insulting Turkishness" to silence a number of prominent Turkish intellectuals who spoke of atrocities suffered by Armenians in the last days of the Ottoman Empire (most of these cases have been dismissed).<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[256]</a></sup> During a February 2005 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Das_Magazin" class="mw-redirect" title="Das Magazin">Das Magazin</a></i>, novelist <a href="/wiki/Orhan_Pamuk" title="Orhan Pamuk">Orhan Pamuk</a> made statements implicating Turkey in massacres against Armenians and persecution of the Kurds, declaring: "Thirty thousand Kurds and a million Armenians were killed in these lands and nobody but me dares to talk about it". Subjected to a <a href="/wiki/Hate_speech" title="Hate speech">hate campaign</a>, he left Turkey, before returning in 2005 to defend his right to <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a>: "What happened to the Ottoman Armenians in 1915 was a major thing that was hidden from the Turkish nation; it was a taboo. But we have to be able to talk about the past".<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[257]</a></sup> Lawyers of two Turkish ultranationalist professional associations led by <a href="/wiki/Kemal_Kerin%C3%A7siz" title="Kemal Kerinçsiz">Kemal Kerinçsiz</a> then brought criminal charges against Pamuk.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[258]</a></sup> However, on 23 January 2006 the charges of "insulting Turkishness" were dropped (for reasons not necessarily tied to the case), a move welcomed by the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[259]</a></sup> However, the fact that the charges had been brought at all was still a matter of contention for European politicians.</p>
<p>These prosecutions have often been accompanied by hate campaigns and threats, as was the case for <a href="/wiki/Hrant_Dink" title="Hrant Dink">Hrant Dink</a>, who was prosecuted three times for "<a href="/wiki/Article_301_(Turkish_penal_code)" class="mw-redirect" title="Article 301 (Turkish penal code)">insulting Turkishness</a>", and murdered in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[260]</a></sup> Later, photographs of the assassin being honored as a hero while in police custody, posing in front of the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish flag">Turkish flag</a> with grinning policemen,<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[261]</a></sup> gave the academic community still more cause for pause with regard to engaging the Armenian issue.<sup id="cite_ref-IPI070122_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPI070122-265">[262]</a></sup> Kerinçsiz, the leading lawyer behind the prosecutions, has been accused of plotting to overthrow the government as a member of the alleged <a href="/wiki/Ergenekon_network" class="mw-redirect" title="Ergenekon network">Ergenekon network</a>.</p>
<p>After a meeting with then UK Prime Minister Gordon Brown in 2010, Turkey's prime minister announced that the Turkish government might order the expulsion of all illegal Armenian immigrants from Turkey. The statement came after recent US House Committee and Swedish Parliament resolutions over the Armenian Genocide affirmation. He repeated the statement in a BBC interview immediately afterwards, declaring that there were 100,000 illegal Armenian citizens living in Turkey and that:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>If necessary, I may have to tell these 100,000 to go back to their country because they are not my citizens. I don't have to keep them in my country.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[263]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph-100.2C000_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-100.2C000-267">[264]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Armenian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Tigran_Sargsyan" title="Tigran Sargsyan">Tigran Sargsyan</a> responded to Erdoğan's statement by saying that this kind of threat reminded Armenians of the Armenian Genocide and that it does not improve relations between the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[265]</a></sup> The exact number of illegal Armenians in Turkey is estimated to be only 12,000–13,000, contrary to the figure used by Erdoğan.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[266]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Republic_of_Armenia_and_the_Genocide">The Republic of Armenia and the Genocide</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="Nagorno-Karabakh War">Nagorno-Karabakh War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sumgait_pogrom" title="Sumgait pogrom">Sumgait pogrom</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D4%BE%D5%AB%D5%AE%D5%A5%D5%BC%D5%B6%D5%A1%D5%AF%D5%A1%D5%A2%D5%A5%D6%80%D5%A4%D5%AB_%D5%B0%D5%B8%D6%82%D5%B7%D5%A1%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B4%D5%A1%D5%AC%D5%AB%D6%80_%D4%B1%D5%BA%D6%80%D5%AB%D5%AC%D5%AB_24-%D5%AB%D5%B6_(12).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/%D4%BE%D5%AB%D5%AE%D5%A5%D5%BC%D5%B6%D5%A1%D5%AF%D5%A1%D5%A2%D5%A5%D6%80%D5%A4%D5%AB_%D5%B0%D5%B8%D6%82%D5%B7%D5%A1%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B4%D5%A1%D5%AC%D5%AB%D6%80_%D4%B1%D5%BA%D6%80%D5%AB%D5%AC%D5%AB_24-%D5%AB%D5%B6_%2812%29.JPG/220px-%D4%BE%D5%AB%D5%AE%D5%A5%D5%BC%D5%B6%D5%A1%D5%AF%D5%A1%D5%A2%D5%A5%D6%80%D5%A4%D5%AB_%D5%B0%D5%B8%D6%82%D5%B7%D5%A1%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B4%D5%A1%D5%AC%D5%AB%D6%80_%D4%B1%D5%BA%D6%80%D5%AB%D5%AC%D5%AB_24-%D5%AB%D5%B6_%2812%29.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/%D4%BE%D5%AB%D5%AE%D5%A5%D5%BC%D5%B6%D5%A1%D5%AF%D5%A1%D5%A2%D5%A5%D6%80%D5%A4%D5%AB_%D5%B0%D5%B8%D6%82%D5%B7%D5%A1%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B4%D5%A1%D5%AC%D5%AB%D6%80_%D4%B1%D5%BA%D6%80%D5%AB%D5%AC%D5%AB_24-%D5%AB%D5%B6_%2812%29.JPG/330px-%D4%BE%D5%AB%D5%AE%D5%A5%D5%BC%D5%B6%D5%A1%D5%AF%D5%A1%D5%A2%D5%A5%D6%80%D5%A4%D5%AB_%D5%B0%D5%B8%D6%82%D5%B7%D5%A1%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B4%D5%A1%D5%AC%D5%AB%D6%80_%D4%B1%D5%BA%D6%80%D5%AB%D5%AC%D5%AB_24-%D5%AB%D5%B6_%2812%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/%D4%BE%D5%AB%D5%AE%D5%A5%D5%BC%D5%B6%D5%A1%D5%AF%D5%A1%D5%A2%D5%A5%D6%80%D5%A4%D5%AB_%D5%B0%D5%B8%D6%82%D5%B7%D5%A1%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B4%D5%A1%D5%AC%D5%AB%D6%80_%D4%B1%D5%BA%D6%80%D5%AB%D5%AC%D5%AB_24-%D5%AB%D5%B6_%2812%29.JPG/440px-%D4%BE%D5%AB%D5%AE%D5%A5%D5%BC%D5%B6%D5%A1%D5%AF%D5%A1%D5%A2%D5%A5%D6%80%D5%A4%D5%AB_%D5%B0%D5%B8%D6%82%D5%B7%D5%A1%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B4%D5%A1%D5%AC%D5%AB%D6%80_%D4%B1%D5%BA%D6%80%D5%AB%D5%AC%D5%AB_24-%D5%AB%D5%B6_%2812%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D4%BE%D5%AB%D5%AE%D5%A5%D5%BC%D5%B6%D5%A1%D5%AF%D5%A1%D5%A2%D5%A5%D6%80%D5%A4%D5%AB_%D5%B0%D5%B8%D6%82%D5%B7%D5%A1%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B4%D5%A1%D5%AC%D5%AB%D6%80_%D4%B1%D5%BA%D6%80%D5%AB%D5%AC%D5%AB_24-%D5%AB%D5%B6_(12).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide_Remembrance_Day" title="Armenian Genocide Remembrance Day">Armenian Genocide Remembrance Day</a> is a national holiday in Armenia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> has been involved in a protracted ethnic-territorial conflict with <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a> state, since Azerbaijan became independent from the Soviet Union in 1991. The conflict has featured several pogroms, massacres, and waves of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a>, by both sides. Some foreign policy observers and historians have suggested that Armenia and the Armenian diaspora have sought to portray the modern conflict as a continuation of the Armenian Genocide, in order to influence modern policy-making in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloxham_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloxham-119">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ambrosio12_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ambrosio12-270">[267]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:232–3</sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Ambrosio" title="Thomas Ambrosio">Thomas Ambrosio</a>, the Armenian Genocide furnishes "a reserve of public sympathy and moral legitimacy that translates into significant political influence&#160;... to elicit congressional support for anti-Azerbaijan policies".<sup id="cite_ref-ambrosio12_270-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ambrosio12-270">[267]</a></sup></p>
<p>The rhetoric leading up to the onset of the conflict, which unfolded in the context of several pogroms of Armenians, was dominated by references to the Armenian Genocide, including fears that it would be, or was in the course of being, repeated.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[268]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[269]</a></sup> During the conflict, the Azeri and Armenian governments regularly accused each other of genocidal intent, although these claims have been treated skeptically by outside observers.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloxham_119-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloxham-119">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:232–33</sup></p>
<p>The worldwide recognition of the Genocide is a core aspect of Armenia's foreign policy and overarching grand strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[270]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_loss">Cultural loss</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Varagavank_view_Bachmann_1913.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Varagavank_view_Bachmann_1913.png/220px-Varagavank_view_Bachmann_1913.png" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Varagavank_view_Bachmann_1913.png/330px-Varagavank_view_Bachmann_1913.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Varagavank_view_Bachmann_1913.png/440px-Varagavank_view_Bachmann_1913.png 2x" data-file-width="1507" data-file-height="1002" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Varagavank_view_Bachmann_1913.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Varagavank" title="Varagavank">Varagavank</a> monastery in Van (1913), burned and destroyed by the Turkish army in May 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-K.C3.A9vorkian_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-K.C3.A9vorkian-274">[271]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Armenian_cultural_heritage_in_Turkey" title="Armenian cultural heritage in Turkey">Armenian cultural heritage in Turkey</a></div>
<p>The premeditated destruction of objects of Armenian cultural, religious, historical and communal heritage was yet another key purpose of both the genocide itself and the post-genocidal campaign of denial. Armenian churches and monasteries were destroyed or changed into mosques, Armenian cemeteries flattened, and, in several cities (e.g., Van), Armenian quarters were demolished.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[272]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aside from the deaths, Armenians lost their wealth and property without compensation.<sup id="cite_ref-TottenParsons2004_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TottenParsons2004-276">[273]</a></sup> Businesses and farms were lost, and all schools, churches, hospitals, orphanages, monasteries, and graveyards became Turkish state property.<sup id="cite_ref-TottenParsons2004_276-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TottenParsons2004-276">[273]</a></sup> In January 1916, the Ottoman Minister of Commerce and Agriculture issued a decree ordering all financial institutions operating within the empire's borders to turn over Armenian assets to the government.<sup id="cite_ref-Business_Wire_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Business_Wire-277">[274]</a></sup> It is recorded that as much as six million Turkish gold pounds were seized along with real property, cash, bank deposits, and jewelry.<sup id="cite_ref-Business_Wire_277-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Business_Wire-277">[274]</a></sup> The assets were then funneled to European banks, including <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dresdner_Bank" title="Dresdner Bank">Dresdner</a> banks.<sup id="cite_ref-Business_Wire_277-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Business_Wire-277">[274]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the end of World War I, Genocide survivors tried to return and reclaim their former homes and assets, but were driven out by the <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Ankara Government">Ankara Government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TottenParsons2004_276-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TottenParsons2004-276">[273]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1914, the Armenian Patriarch in Constantinople presented a list of the Armenian holy sites under his supervision. The list contained 2,549 religious places of which 200 were monasteries while 1,600 were churches. In 1974 UNESCO stated that after 1923, out of 913 Armenian historical monuments left in Eastern Turkey, 464 have vanished completely, 252 are in ruins, and 197 are in need of repair (in stable conditions).<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[275]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[276]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reparations_to_the_victims">Reparations to the victims</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide_reparations" title="Armenian Genocide reparations">Armenian Genocide reparations</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reparations_on_the_grounds_of_international_law">Reparations on the grounds of international law</span></h3>
<p>The United Nations Basic Principles and Guidelines on the Right to Reparation for Victims of Gross Violations of Human Rights and International Humanitarian Law provide in part, that reparation may be claimed individually and where appropriate collectively, by the direct victims of violations of human rights and international humanitarian law, the immediate family, dependants or other persons or groups of persons closely connected with the direct victims.<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCR_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCR-280">[277]</a></sup> According to Henry Theriault, while current members of Turkish society cannot be blamed morally for the destruction of Armenians, present-day <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Turkey">Republic of Turkey</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Successor_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Successor state">successor state</a> to the Ottoman Empire and as beneficiary of the wealth and land expropriations brought forth through the genocide, is responsible for reparations.<sup id="cite_ref-Theriault_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Theriault-281">[278]</a></sup></p>
<p>Particularly important are Principles 9 and 12 that state, that civil claims relating to reparations for gross violations of human rights and international humanitarian law shall not be subject to statutes of limitations (article 9), and that restitution shall be provided to re-establish the situation that existed prior to the violations of human rights or international humanitarian law. The restitution requires, <i>inter alia</i> – return to one's place of residence and restoration of property.<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCR_280-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCR-280">[277]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[279]</a></sup></p>
<p>Professor of International Law of <a href="/wiki/Geneva_School_of_Diplomacy" class="mw-redirect" title="Geneva School of Diplomacy">Geneva School of Diplomacy</a> (J.D. – Harvard, Dr.phil. – Göttingen), former Secretary of the <a href="/wiki/UN_Human_Rights_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Human Rights Committee">UN Human Rights Committee</a> and former Chief of Petitions at the Office of the <a href="/wiki/UN_High_Commissioner_for_Human_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="UN High Commissioner for Human Rights">UN High Commissioner for Human Rights</a>, Dr. Alfred de Zayas stated that, because of the continuing character of the crime of genocide in factual and legal terms, the remedy of restitution has not been foreclosed. Thus the survivors of the genocide against the Armenians, both individually and collectively, have standing to advance a claim for restitution. Whenever possible complete restitution or restoration to the previous condition should be granted. But where it is not possible, relevant compensation may be substituted as a remedy. <sup id="cite_ref-Alfred_de_Zayas_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alfred_de_Zayas-283">[280]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an article published in the <a href="/wiki/European_Journal_of_International_Law" title="European Journal of International Law">European Journal of International Law</a>, Vahagn Avedian, leaving aside the limitations of the UN Genocide Convention, emphasizes the applicability of international laws that prevailed at the time and remain in force up to the present, e.g. the <a href="/wiki/Hague_Conventions_of_1899_and_1907" title="Hague Conventions of 1899 and 1907">Hague Conventions of 1899 and 1907</a>, more specifically the <a href="/wiki/Martens_Clause" title="Martens Clause">Martens Clause</a>, pertaining to the protection of civilian population, but also existing international laws on unlawful confiscation, etc. Thus, the actions of the Turkish governments (the Ottoman, the insurgent nationalist movement as well as the succeeding republic), should be viewed from the perspective of Internationally Wrongful Acts. Avedian argues that:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>the Republic not only failed to stop doing the wrongful acts of its predecessor, but it also continued the very internationally wrongful acts committed by the Young Turk government. Thus, the insurgent National Movement, which later became the Republic, made itself responsible for not only its own wrongful acts but also those of its predecessor, including the act of genocide committed in 1915–1916.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[281]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="S.C3.A8vres_Treaty">Sèvres Treaty</span></h3>
<p>Although there are different opinions on the legitimacy of the Treaty of Sèvres and its relativity to reparation claims, there are specialists who claim that some of its elements retain the force of law.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[282]</a></sup> In particular, the fixing of the proper borders of an Armenian state was undertaken pursuant to the treaty and determined by a binding arbitral award, regardless of whether the treaty was ultimately ratified. <i>The committee process determining the arbitral award was agreed to by the parties</i> and, according to international law, the resulting determination has legal force regardless of the ultimate fate of the treaty.<sup id="cite_ref-Theriault_281-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Theriault-281">[278]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lawsuits">Lawsuits</span></h3>
<p>In July 2004, after the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Legislature" title="California State Legislature">California State Legislature</a> passed the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Armenian_Genocide_Insurance_Act&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Armenian Genocide Insurance Act (page does not exist)">Armenian Genocide Insurance Act</a>, descendants of Armenian Genocide victims settled a case for about 2,400 life insurance policies from <a href="/wiki/New_York_Life" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Life">New York Life</a> written on Armenians living in the Ottoman Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-Reparations_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reparations-286">[283]</a></sup> Around 1918, the Turkish government attempted to recover payments for the people it had killed, with the argument that there were no identifiable heirs to the policy holders. The settlement provided $20 million, of which $11 million was for heirs of the Genocide victims.<sup id="cite_ref-Reparations_286-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reparations-286">[283]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commemoration">Commemoration</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Armenian_Genocide_Memorial_-_Yerevan_(2903020364).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Armenian_Genocide_Memorial_-_Yerevan_%282903020364%29.jpg/220px-Armenian_Genocide_Memorial_-_Yerevan_%282903020364%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Armenian_Genocide_Memorial_-_Yerevan_%282903020364%29.jpg/330px-Armenian_Genocide_Memorial_-_Yerevan_%282903020364%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Armenian_Genocide_Memorial_-_Yerevan_%282903020364%29.jpg/440px-Armenian_Genocide_Memorial_-_Yerevan_%282903020364%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1872" data-file-height="1247" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Armenian_Genocide_Memorial_-_Yerevan_(2903020364).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Armenian Genocide Memorial on the hill of <a href="/wiki/Tsitsernakaberd" title="Tsitsernakaberd">Tsitsernakaberd</a> (Yerevan)</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Memorials">Memorials</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Armenian_Genocide_memorials" title="List of Armenian Genocide memorials">List of Armenian Genocide memorials</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_visitors_to_Tsitsernakaberd" title="List of visitors to Tsitsernakaberd">List of visitors to Tsitsernakaberd</a></div>
<p>Over 135 memorials, spread across 25 countries, commemorate the Armenian Genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[284]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1965, the 50th anniversary of the genocide, a <a href="/wiki/1965_Yerevan_demonstrations" title="1965 Yerevan demonstrations">24-hour mass protest</a> was initiated in <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a> demanding recognition of the Armenian Genocide by Soviet authorities. The memorial was completed two years later, at <a href="/wiki/Tsitsernakaberd" title="Tsitsernakaberd">Tsitsernakaberd</a> above the <a href="/wiki/Hrazdan" title="Hrazdan">Hrazdan</a> gorge in Yerevan. The 44 metres (144&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Stela" class="mw-redirect" title="Stela">stele</a> symbolizes the national rebirth of Armenians. Twelve slabs are positioned in a circle, representing 12&#160;lost provinces in present-day Turkey. At the center of the circle there is an <a href="/wiki/Eternal_flame" title="Eternal flame">eternal flame</a>. Each 24 April, hundreds of thousands of people walk to the monument, which is the official memorial of the genocide, and lay flowers around the eternal flame.<cite class="citation book">Freedman, Jeri (2009). <i>The Armenian genocide</i>. New York: Rosen Pub. Group. p.&#160;49. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-4042-1825-4" title="Special:BookSources/1-4042-1825-4">1-4042-1825-4</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArmenian+Genocide&amp;rft.aufirst=Jeri&amp;rft.aulast=Freedman&amp;rft.btitle=The+Armenian+genocide&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=1-4042-1825-4&amp;rft.pages=49&amp;rft.place=New+York&amp;rft.pub=Rosen+Pub.+Group&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></p>
<p>Another memorial, in <a href="/wiki/Alfortville" title="Alfortville">Alfortville</a>, France, near Paris, was bombed on 3 May 1984, by a hit-team headed by <a href="/wiki/Grey_Wolves_(organization)" title="Grey Wolves (organization)">Grey Wolves</a> member <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_%C3%87atl%C4%B1" title="Abdullah Çatlı">Abdullah Çatlı</a> and paid by the <a href="/wiki/National_Intelligence_Organization_(Turkey)" title="National Intelligence Organization (Turkey)">Turkish intelligence agency (MİT)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Zaman_Ergenekon_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zaman_Ergenekon-288">[285]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portrayal_in_the_media">Portrayal in the media</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide_in_culture" title="Armenian Genocide in culture">Armenian Genocide in culture</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div id="mwe_player_4" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; style=&quot;width:400px&quot;&gt;&lt;video id=&quot;mwe_player_5&quot; poster=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Ravished_Armenia_FULL_MOVIE.ogv/400px--Ravished_Armenia_FULL_MOVIE.ogv.jpg&quot; <div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ravished_Armenia_FULL_MOVIE.ogv" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"Ravished Armenia" (also called "Auction of Souls")</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first artwork known to have been influenced by the Armenian Genocide was a medal struck in St. Petersburg while the massacres and deportations of 1915 were at their height. It was issued as a token of Russian sympathy for Armenian suffering. Since then, dozens of similar medals have been commissioned in various countries.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[286]</a></sup></p>
<p>Numerous eyewitness accounts of the atrocities were published, notably those of Swedish missionary <a href="/wiki/Alma_Johansson" title="Alma Johansson">Alma Johansson</a> and U.S. Ambassador <a href="/wiki/Henry_Morgenthau,_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Morgenthau, Sr.">Henry Morgenthau, Sr.</a> German medic <a href="/wiki/Armin_Wegner" class="mw-redirect" title="Armin Wegner">Armin Wegner</a> wrote several books about the atrocities he witnessed while stationed in the Ottoman Empire. Years later, having returned to Germany, Wegner was imprisoned for opposing <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[287]</a></sup> and his books were <a href="/wiki/Nazi_book_burning" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi book burning">burnt</a> by the Nazis.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[288]</a></sup> Probably the best known literary work on the Armenian Genocide is <a href="/wiki/Franz_Werfel" title="Franz Werfel">Franz Werfel</a>'s 1933 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Forty_Days_of_Musa_Dagh" title="The Forty Days of Musa Dagh">The Forty Days of Musa Dagh</a></i>. It was a bestseller that became particularly popular among the youth in the Jewish ghettos during the Nazi era.<sup id="cite_ref-Auron_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auron-91">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:302–4</sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kurt_Vonnegut" title="Kurt Vonnegut">Kurt Vonnegut</a>'s 1988 novel <i><a href="/wiki/Bluebeard_(book)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bluebeard (book)">Bluebeard</a></i> features the Armenian Genocide as an underlying theme. Other novels incorporating the Armenian Genocide include <a href="/wiki/Louis_de_Berni%C3%A9res" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis de Berniéres">Louis de Berniéres</a>' <i>Birds without Wings</i>, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Hilsenrath" title="Edgar Hilsenrath">Edgar Hilsenrath</a>'s German-language <i><a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_the_Last_Thought" title="The Story of the Last Thought">The Story of the Last Thought</a></i>, and Polish <a href="/wiki/Stefan_%C5%BBeromski" title="Stefan Żeromski">Stefan Żeromski</a>'s 1925 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spring_to_Come" title="The Spring to Come">The Spring to Come</a></i>. A story in Edward Saint-Ivan's 2006 anthology "The Black Knight's God" includes a fictional survivor of the Armenian Genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[289]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first film about the Armenian Genocide appeared in 1919, a Hollywood production titled <i><a href="/wiki/Ravished_Armenia" title="Ravished Armenia">Ravished Armenia</a></i>. It was produced by the <a href="/wiki/American_Committee_for_Armenian_and_Syrian_Relief" class="mw-redirect" title="American Committee for Armenian and Syrian Relief">American Committee for Armenian and Syrian Relief</a> and was based on the narrative account of survivor <a href="/wiki/Aurora_Mardiganian" title="Aurora Mardiganian">Aurora Mardiganian</a>, who played herself. It resonated with acclaimed director <a href="/wiki/Atom_Egoyan" title="Atom Egoyan">Atom Egoyan</a>, influencing his 2002 <i><a href="/wiki/Ararat_(film)" title="Ararat (film)">Ararat</a></i>. There are also references in <a href="/wiki/Elia_Kazan" title="Elia Kazan">Elia Kazan</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/America,_America" class="mw-redirect" title="America, America">America, America</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Henri_Verneuil" title="Henri Verneuil">Henri Verneuil</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Mayrig" title="Mayrig">Mayrig</a></i>. At the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_International_Film_Festival" title="Berlin International Film Festival">Berlin International Film Festival</a> of 2007 Italian directors <a href="/wiki/Paolo_and_Vittorio_Taviani" title="Paolo and Vittorio Taviani">Paolo and Vittorio Taviani</a> presented another film about the atrocities, based on Antonia Arslan's book, <i><a href="/wiki/La_Masseria_Delle_Allodole" class="mw-redirect" title="La Masseria Delle Allodole">La Masseria Delle Allodole</a></i> (<i>The Farm of the Larks</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[290]</a></sup> Richard Kalinoski's play, <i>Beast on the Moon</i>, is about two Armenian Genocide survivors.</p>
<p>The paintings of Armenian-American <a href="/wiki/Arshile_Gorky" title="Arshile Gorky">Arshile Gorky</a>, a seminal figure of <a href="/wiki/Abstract_Expressionism" class="mw-redirect" title="Abstract Expressionism">Abstract Expressionism</a>, are considered to have been influenced by the suffering and loss of the period.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[291]</a></sup> In 1915, at age 10, Gorky fled his native <a href="/wiki/Van,_Turkey" title="Van, Turkey">Van</a> and escaped to Russian-Armenia with his mother and three sisters, only to have his mother die of starvation in Yerevan in 1919. His two <i>The Artist and His Mother</i> paintings are based on a photograph with his mother taken in Van.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Artist_and_His_Mother.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a5/The_Artist_and_His_Mother.jpg/170px-The_Artist_and_His_Mother.jpg" width="170" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a5/The_Artist_and_His_Mother.jpg/255px-The_Artist_and_His_Mother.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/a5/The_Artist_and_His_Mother.jpg 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="362" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Artist_and_His_Mother.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Arshile_Gorky" title="Arshile Gorky">Arshile Gorky</a>'s <i>The Artist and His Mother</i> (ca. 1926–36)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1975, famous French-Armenian singer <a href="/wiki/Charles_Aznavour" title="Charles Aznavour">Charles Aznavour</a> recorded the song "<a href="/wiki/Ils_Sont_Tomb%C3%A9s_(Charles_Aznavour_Song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ils Sont Tombés (Charles Aznavour Song)">Ils sont tombés</a>" ("They Fell"), dedicated to the memory of Armenian Genocide victims.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[292]</a></sup></p>
<p>The American band <a href="/wiki/System_of_a_Down" title="System of a Down">System of a Down</a>, composed of four descendants of Armenian Genocide survivors, has promoted awareness of the Armenian Genocide through its lyrics, including <a href="/w/index.php?title=P.L.U.C.K.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="P.L.U.C.K. (page does not exist)">P.L.U.C.K.</a> and in concerts.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[293]</a></sup> On April 23, 2015, the band performed a free concert in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_Square,_Yerevan" title="Republic Square, Yerevan">Republic Square, Yerevan</a>, to commemorate the 100th anniversary of the genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[294]</a></sup></p>
<p>In late 2003, <a href="/wiki/Diamanda_Gal%C3%A1s" title="Diamanda Galás">Diamanda Galás</a> released the album <i>Defixiones, Will and Testament: Orders from the Dead</i>, an 80-minute memorial tribute to the Armenian, Assyrian and Greek victims of the genocide in Turkey. "The performance is an angry meditation on genocide and the politically cooperative denial of it, in particular the Turkish and American denial of the Armenian, Assyrian, and Anatolian Greek genocides from 1914 to 1923".<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[295]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008, Armenian-American composer <a href="/wiki/Andrey_Kasparov" title="Andrey Kasparov">Andrey Kasparov</a> premiered <i>Tsitsernakabert</i>, an original work for modern dance and six musicians: alto flute, bass/ contrabass flute, violin, two percussionists, and mezzo-soprano.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[296]</a></sup> The work opens with eight dancers posed in a circle – inclined toward the circle's centre – in a tableau reminiscent of the <a href="/wiki/Tsitsernakaberd" title="Tsitsernakaberd">eponymous memorial</a> to victims of the Armenian Genocide, situated in <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a>, capital of <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[297]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[298]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Julian_Cope" title="Julian Cope">Julian Cope</a>'s 2013 album <i><a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Suicide_(album)" title="Revolutionary Suicide (album)">Revolutionary Suicide</a></i> includes a song over 15 minutes long, "The Armenian Genocide", memorializing the event.</p>
<p>The 2014 drama film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cut_(2014_film)" title="The Cut (2014 film)">The Cut</a></i> is based on the Armenian Genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[299]</a></sup></p>
<p>Argentine composer <a href="/wiki/Juan_Mar%C3%ADa_Solare" title="Juan María Solare">Juan María Solare</a> wrote a lyrical <a href="/wiki/Monodrama" title="Monodrama">monodrama</a> titled <i>Verchin Oror</i> (Last Lullaby), with text by <a href="/wiki/Ruben_Sevak" title="Ruben Sevak">Ruben Sevak</a> (1885–1915), one of the poets arrested on 24 April 1915. This work (symbolically finished on 24 April 2015) was a commission of the Foundation Encuentros Internacionales de Música Contemporánea (Argentina). The piece is scored for mezzo-soprano and instrumental quintet (flute, clarinet, violin, cello and piano).</p>
<p>On 13 April 2015, <a href="/wiki/1915_The_Movie" class="mw-redirect" title="1915 The Movie">1915 The Movie</a> held its Hollywood premiere at the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Theater" class="mw-redirect" title="Egyptian Theater">Egyptian Theater</a> in Los Angeles. The film was screened across the world, including Canada, Russia, and Armenia. Directed by <a href="/wiki/Garin_Hovannisian" title="Garin Hovannisian">Garin Hovannisian</a> and Alec Mouhibian, the film tells the story of a mysterious director (played by <a href="/wiki/Simon_Abkarian" title="Simon Abkarian">Simon Abkarian</a>), who stages a play and intends to bring the ghosts of the Armenian Genocide back.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[300]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Armenian Genocide is generally associated with 1915, the year that most of the atrocities took place. The span varies from source to source: 1915–1916, 1915–1917, 1915–1918, 1915–1923, 1894–1915, 1894–1923</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-fatalities-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-fatalities_12-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fatalities_12-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">1.5 million is the most published number,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> however, estimates vary from 800,000 to 1,800,000<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auron2000_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auron2000-9">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forsythe2009_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forsythe2009-10">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ChalkJonassohn1990_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChalkJonassohn1990-11">[10]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Հայոց ցեղասպանութիւն in <a href="/wiki/Classical_Armenian_orthography" title="Classical Armenian orthography">classical Armenian orthography</a></span></li>
</ol>

<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation"><i>Armenian Genocide</i> (affirmation), The International Association of Genocide Scholars, <q>That this assembly of the Association of Genocide Scholars in its conference held in Montreal, June 11–13, 1997, reaffirms that the mass murder of Armenians in Turkey in 1915 is a case of genocide which conforms to the statutes of the United Nations Convention on the Prevention and Punishment of Genocide. It further condemns the denial of the Armenian Genocide by the Turkish government and its official and unofficial agents and supporters.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArmenian+Genocide&amp;rft.btitle=Armenian+Genocide&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.pub=The+International+Association+of+Genocide+Scholars&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-46">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation">"Article 16", <i><a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_San_Stefano" title="Treaty of San Stefano">Treaty of San Stefano</a></i>, <q>As the evacuation of the Russian troops of the territory they occupy in Armenia&#160;... might give rise to conflicts and complications detrimental to the maintenance of good relations between the two countries, the <a href="/wiki/Sublime_Porte" title="Sublime Porte">Sublime Porte</a> engaged to carry into effect, without further delay, the improvements and reforms demanded by local requirements in the provinces inhabited by Armenians and to guarantee their security from Kurds and <a href="/wiki/Circassians" title="Circassians">Circassians</a>.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArmenian+Genocide&amp;rft.atitle=Article+16&amp;rft.btitle=Treaty+of+San+Stefano&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
