<li id="cite_note-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-49">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.history.com/topics/armenian-genocide">"Armenian Genocide"</a>. <i>history.com</i>. <a href="/wiki/History_(U.S._TV_channel)" title="History (U.S. TV channel)">History</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArmenian+Genocide&amp;rft.atitle=Armenian+Genocide&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.history.com%2Ftopics%2Farmenian-genocide&amp;rft.jtitle=history.com&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The German Foreign Ministry operative, Ernst Jackh, estimated that 200,000 Armenians were killed and a further 50,000 expelled from the provinces during the Hamidian unrest. French diplomats placed the figures at 250,000 killed. The German pastor <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Lepsius" title="Johannes Lepsius">Johannes Lepsius</a> was more meticulous in his calculations, counting the deaths of 88,000&#160;Armenians and the destruction of 2,500&#160;villages, 645&#160;churches and monasteries, and the plundering of hundreds of churches, of which 328 were converted into mosques.</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-Whitehorn2015-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Whitehorn2015_62-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Alan Whitehorn (26 May 2015). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=0vrnCQAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA139"><i>The Armenian Genocide: The Essential Reference Guide</i></a>. ABC-CLIO. p.&#160;139. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-61069-688-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-61069-688-3">978-1-61069-688-3</a>. <q>That particular date was chosen because on April 24, 1915, the Ottoman Young Turk government began deporting hundreds of Armenian leaders and intellectuals from Constantinople (Istanbul); most were later murdered en masse.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArmenian+Genocide&amp;rft.au=Alan+Whitehorn&amp;rft.btitle=The+Armenian+Genocide%3A+The+Essential+Reference+Guide&amp;rft.date=2015-05-26&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D0vrnCQAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPA139&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-61069-688-3&amp;rft.pages=139&amp;rft.pub=ABC-CLIO&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-Dad360-361-138"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Dad360-361_138-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">These are according to the figures provided by <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Myasnikyan" class="mw-redirect" title="Aleksandr Myasnikyan">Alexander Miasnikyan</a>, the President of the Council of People's Commissars of Soviet Armenia, in a telegram he sent to the Soviet Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Chicherin" title="Georgy Chicherin">Georgy Chicherin</a> in 1921. Miasnikyan's figures were broken down as follows: of the approximately 60,000 Armenians who were killed by the Turkish armies, 30,000 were men, 15,000 women, 5,000 children, and 10,000 young girls. Of the 38,000 who were wounded, 20,000 were men, 10,000 women, 5,000 young girls, and 3,000 children. Instances of mass rape, murder and violence were also reported against the Armenian populace of Kars and Alexandropol: see <a href="/wiki/Vahakn_N._Dadrian" class="mw-redirect" title="Vahakn N. Dadrian">Vahakn N. Dadrian</a>. (2003). <i>The History of the Armenian Genocide: Ethnic Conflict from the Balkans to Anatolia to the Caucasus</i>. New York: Berghahn Books, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=ZCVJMAVoMM0C&amp;pg=PA360">pp. 360–61</a>. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1571816666" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1-57181-666-6</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-139"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-139">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Armenia&#160;: The Survival of a Nation, Christopher Walker, 1980.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-H.RES.316-140"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-H.RES.316_140-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">1915 declaration</span>

Cambridge University Press, 2000. p. 25: "Lemkin's interest in the subject dates to his days as a student at Lvov University, when he intently followed attempts to prosecute the perpetration of the massacres of the Armenians"</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-Moses2004-197"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Moses2004_197-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Dirk Moses, A. (2004). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=5zHAGNPTkqIC&amp;pg=PA21"><i>Genocide and Settler Society: Frontier Violence and Stolen Indigenous Children in Australian History</i></a>. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">15 April</span> 2016</span>. <q>Indignant that the perpetrators of the Armenian genocide had largely escaped prosecution, Lemkin, who was a young state prosecutor in Poland, began lobbying in the early 1930s for international law to criminalize the destruction of such groups.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArmenian+Genocide&amp;rft.aufirst=A.&amp;rft.aulast=Dirk+Moses&amp;rft.btitle=Genocide+and+Settler+Society%3A+Frontier+Violence+and+Stolen+Indigenous+Children+in+Australian+History&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D5zHAGNPTkqIC%26pg%3DPA21&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-57181-410-4&amp;rft.pages=21&amp;rft.pub=Berghahn+Books&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-ushmm-198"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ushmm_198-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20100615174207/http://www.ushmm.org/wlc/en/article.php?ModuleId=10007050">"Coining a Word and Championing a Cause: The Story of Raphael Lemkin"</a>. <li id="cite_note-201"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-201">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"The relationship between the Armenian Genocide and the Holocaust is apparent in two periods of history. The first is the debate that raged in Germany regarding the slaughter of Armenians by its ally the Ottoman Empire in the early 1920s. The debate came down in favor of genocide, and by the time the Nazis came to power, violence against the Armenians had been understood and even outright justified, already for decades. The second period is when the Nazis were in power and looked to the post-ethnic cleansing Turkey as a role model."; Ihrig, Stefan; How the Armenian Genocide Shaped the Holocaust; 2016; <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.thedailybeast.com/articles/2016/01/24/how-the-armenian-genocide-shaped-the-holocaust.html">http://www.thedailybeast.com/articles/2016/01/24/how-the-armenian-genocide-shaped-the-holocaust.html</a></span></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_overviews">Historical overviews</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Taner_Ak%C3%A7am" title="Taner Akçam">Akçam, Taner</a>. <i>A Shameful Act: The Armenian Genocide and the Question of Turkish Responsibility</i>. New York: Metropolitan Books, 2007.</li>
<li><cite id="CITEREFAk.C3.A7am2012" class="citation book">Akçam, Taner (2012). <i>The Young Turks' Crime Against Humanity: The Armenian Genocide and Ethnic Cleansing in the Ottoman Empire</i>. Princeton University Press. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-691-15333-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-691-15333-9">978-0-691-15333-9</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArmenian+Genocide&amp;rft.aufirst=Taner&amp;rft.aulast=Ak%C3%A7am&amp;rft.btitle=The+Young+Turks%27+Crime+Against+Humanity%3A+The+Armenian+Genocide+and+Ethnic+Cleansing+in+the+Ottoman+Empire&amp;rft.date=2012&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-691-15333-9&amp;rft.pub=Princeton+University+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peter_Balakian" title="Peter Balakian">Balakian, Peter</a>. <i>The Burning Tigris: The Armenian Genocide and America's Response</i>. New York: HarperCollins, 2003. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0060198400" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0-06-019840-0</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Donald_Bloxham" title="Donald Bloxham">Bloxham, Donald</a>. <i>The Great Game of Genocide: Imperialism, Nationalism, and the Destruction of the Ottoman Armenians</i>.
